$YUN_KMT_NRA_party$
$YUN_KMT_NRA_party$
The Chinese Syndicalist Party was founded in 1922 by a collection of socialist thinkers inspired by the recent successes of French revolutionaries. It allied with the Kuomintang in 1924 in the First United Front, which allowed them to expand in size and influence within the southern Guangzhou government during the warlord era. Emboldened by the Hong Kong-Canton Strike of 1925, the Chinese Syndicalist Party formed the League of Chinese Syndicalists as a broad umbrella of Chinese socialists not directly associated with the Kuomintang, the high water mark of their movement.\n\nYunnan's Syndicalists organised in Peking University in 1923 Beijing under the tutelage of Li Dazhao. The brothers Wang Fusheng and Wang Desan, along with other leaders such as Li Xin and Yang Qingtian founded the Yunnan Reform Society along with other students. They took part in the May 30th protests that year and renamed the group the New Yunnan (Dian) Society.
The Kuomintang was founded by Dr. Sun Yat-sen after the failure of his unwieldy Tongmenghui. The party took an authoritarian turn when he demanded personal loyalty oaths from all of its members, and drifted in a leftwards, vanguardist direction after the 1924 Reorganisation. Built on Dr. Sun's teachings and cult of personality, the party grew severely divided after his death.
In order to combat the warlords, Dr. Sun demanded the creation of an army purely loyal to the party and the revolution known as the National Revolutionary Army. With the help of military advisors from the Third Internationale, the Whampoa Military Academy was erected in Guangzhou which trained a generation of revolutionary military officers.
CSP-YSB
Chinese Syndicalist Party - Yunnan Special Branch (Zhongguo Gongtuandang - Zhengzhi Baowei Bu Yunnan Fenbu)\n§L$YUN_CSP_intro$\n\nA special branch of the CSP was established to coordinate covert operations in Yunnan. This smaller circle included many political and military operatives trained in Whampoa Military Academy by advisors from the Third Internationale.§!\n
KMT-CRS
Kuomintang - China Revival Society (Guomindang Zhonghua Fuxingshe)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nFollowing the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Hu Zongnan broke off from He Yingqin's First Army, joining Wang's CEC in Europe. In Europe, he connected with fellow Whampoa Alumni He Zhonghan and Deng Wenyi, who shared his disappointment in the state of the Party. Embracing ultra-nationalism and staunch militarism, Hu and the CRS embraced the revolutionary violence of French Sorelians, declaring the bureaucracy of the Party to be the root cause of the Northern Expedition's failure. The failure of the leftist committee's most recent adventure into China has broken their cause, leaving them a shell of what they once were. However, following their adoption into the new Kuomintang government, it seems that they have seen a small revival in popularity. Having dropped the more socialist aspects of their platform in favour of emphasising their commitment to rejuvenating the Party's revolutionary resolve, they have established a friendly partnership with Teng Jie's Blueshirts on the basis of a shared commitment to ultra-nationalistic militarism and totalitarianism.§!\n
CSP-NYS
Chinese Syndicalist Party - New Yunnan Society (Zhongguo Gongtuandang - Xin Dian she)\n§L$YUN_CSP_intro$\n\nThe mainline branch of the New Yunnan Society is also a successor to the leftist Law and Government clique of the Yunnan Kuomintang operating out of the Kunming Law school. Despite heavy suppression, it retains a following among radical students.§!\n
World Society
(New) World Society (Shijie She)\n§LThe World Society enjoys the distinction of being the first organised anarchist organisation (anarchists groups traditionally avoid referring to themselves as parties) in China. Led by the Four Elders (Zhang Renjie, Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, and Cai Yuanpei), these Paris-based anarchists became mentors for many prominent Kuomintang figures. Their influence was eclipsed however by the rise of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, especially as their relationship with other anarchists deteriorated and they were forced to retreat into their positions in the Kuomintang establishment.\n\nAlthough they suffered a further loss in influence within the Party following the Leftist Kuomintang Government's collapse, it seems that they have escaped their string of bad luck following their entry into the new Kuomintang Government. Viewing the CSP as something of a political liability, the Nationalist Government has opted to support the World Society in its capacity as head of the League of Chinese Syndicalists in order to contain their radicalism. Li Shizeng in particular has risen to prominence, ingratiating himself in right-wing circles through his recent thorough criticisms of the promotion of class struggle by KMT leftists as well as the CSP, declaring it detrimental during China's fight against foreign imperialist powers.§!\n
KMT-3AL
Kuomintang - 3rd Army of the National Revolutionary Army (Leftists) (Guomindang-Guomingemingjun Di San Jun (Zuopai))\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\n$YUN_NRA_intro$\n\nThe Third Army is the successor of a few earlier armies aligned with the southern government including the Second National Protection Army and the First National Construction Army. It participated in a mutiny against the Kuomintang after Sun's death in 1925, only to be utterly routed.\n\nIt was then reorganised as the Third Army under Zhu Peide, a Yunnan Kuomintang loyalist. It fought with distinction in the Eastern front of the Northern Expedition against Sun Chuanfang, but was ultimately forced to retreat with the rest of the NRA during the Long March. In Guizhou, the Third Army absorbed smaller Yunnan based military forces under Fan Shisheng and Jin Handing after the Kuomintang reorganised in Guizhou.\n\nThe Third Army harbours a large leftist faction within its ranks led by Zhu De. Although far from the majority, if left unchecked they may soon usurp command of the movement.§!\n
KMT-RCA
Kuomintang - Reorganisation Comrades Association (Moderate Faction) (Guomindang - Gaizutongzhihui (Wenhepai))\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nThe Reorganisation Comrades Association was founded by Chen Gongbo, Gu Mengyu and other Kuomintang leftists to defend the 1924 Reorganisation and later to advance the rule of their champion: Wang Jingwei. Internally, the RCA was divided between the Radicals under Chen, who advocated violent class warfare and Marxism, and the Moderates under Gu who preferred class collaboration.\n\nWang Jingwei's decision to join our government has shattered the RCA with many of the rank and file denouncing him as a sell-out. Chen Gongbo has refrained from directly criticising his friend, but has retreated into the shadows as Wang throws his weight behind Gu Mengyu's wing and emphasised his left-nationalist credentials. The RCA retains some sway within our party, particularly among the civilian bureaucracy, parts of the intelligentsia, and overseas chapters, but it's clear that they are well past their heyday.§!\n

KMT-RC
Revolutionary Committee of the Kuomintang (Zhongguo Guomindang Gemingweiyuanhui)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nThe ultimate (if belated) victors of the Chinese Civil War, Zhang Bojun and Zhu De have emerged as the foremost leaders of the Kuomintang in a stunning upset. Gathering various party leaders, particularly those of their former allies in the Provisional Action Committee, though not forgetting to draw useful cadres from the RCA and even the CSP, Zhang and Zhu have reorganised the party under one Revolutionary Committee under their control. They have promised to heal divisions between the party's factions and chart a third path, their own path, going forward to preserve China's revolutionary values.§!\n
CPWDP
Chinese Peasants and Workers' Democratic Party (Zhongguo Nonggong Minzhu Dang)\n§LWith its progenitor in the original Proto Provisional Action Committee, founded by Zhang Bojun and Tan Pingshan in 1927 as a result of the Northern Expedition's failure, having been co-opted by Song Qingling and Deng Yanda, many believed that the fates of Tan and Zhang would be forever tied to the Kuomintang-PAC mantle. With Tan self-exiling himself to lead the Guangdong regional branch of the PAC, and Zhang folding with Deng and Song, such a fate seemed pre-disclosed.\n\nAnd yet with the manipulation of the political battleground by Zhang and his newfound accomplice Zhu De, the duo have managed to propel themselves into a new landmark Third Way for Chinese Socialism. Participating in discussions with Dangwai such as the China Democratic League and the Chinese Syndicalist Party, Zhang has managed to break free from the chains of the White Sun. Advancing ever onwards, Zhang hopes to lead the nation to a new Democratic Socialist future, one beholden to the people and not committee.§!\n

Choosing a side was not easy, as the young cadets were taught a syncretic programme invoking ultra-nationalism, socialism, Japanese Bushido, Chinese traditionalism, and revolutionary violence. Chiang Kai-shek and Deng Yanda were two of the most influential military men within the Academy, and each founded their own alumni organisation. Many found themselves aligning with Chiang due to personal loyalties but sympathetic to Deng's social and economic teachings.§!\n

KMT-RCF
Kuomintang - Reconstruction Faction (Guomindang - Zaizao hui)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nThe Crown Prince's Clique was a loose collection of (then Mayor of Guangzhou) Sun Fo friends and allies, most of whom were recent graduates of western universities. Liberal, technocratic, and often having ties to wealthy donors of the party, it straddled the line between the factions of the growing party divide. After the Northern Expedition, it more formally coalesced into the Reconstruction Faction in Hawaii. Sun Fo's decision to join our government has brought with him the bulk of the Reconstruction Faction, as well as their powerful Overseas Chinese Commission networks in Southeast Asia and various military officers associated with the India Clique.§!\n
KMT-PSC
Kuomintang - (New) Political Science Clique (Guomindang - (Xin) Zhengxue xì)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nThe first iteration of the Political Science Clique was founded in 1913 by Tongmenghui members who rejected Dr. Sun's demand for personal loyalty oaths after the failure of the Second Revolution against Yuan Shikai. They established the European Affairs Research Society in Tokyo, which later evolved into the Political Science Society in 1916.\n\nRejecting the need for a Northern Expedition to unite China, they worked with southern warlords like Cen Chunxuan and Lu Rongting to topple Sun Yat-sen and his Constitution Protection Government and promote reunification negotiations with the northern Beiyang government. When Sun, with the help of Chen Jiongming, was able to drive Cen and Lu out of Guangdong and Tang Jiyao later drove out the Political Science Clique aligned Governor Gu Pinzhen out of Yunnan, the Old Political Science Clique effectively collapsed.\n\nA New Political Science Clique has emerged from an alliance between Zhang Qun and Yang Yongtai, who formed the New China Construction Society (the formal name of the clique). More loyal to the Kuomintang, or at least more docile, this faction has little in the way of mass movement but instead is built on the extensive personal networks between China's southern banking, intellectual, and bureaucratic elite.§!\n
KMT-PSC
Kuomintang - Political Science Clique (Guomindang - Zhengxue Xi)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nArisen from the ashes, albeit not entirely dead as far as the Beiyang World Order is concerned, the Old Political Science Clique has managed to resuscitate its political relevance in the aftermath of the tumultuous Warlord Era. With its contemporaries within the New China Construction Society ultimately folding under their senior's umbrella, the technocrats of the Party-State have rallied around the legendary war hero, veteran and Political Science stalwart Li Genyuan in the hopes of synthesising their own form of Tutelage.§!\n
KMT-3AR
Kuomintang - 3rd Army of the National Revolutionary Army (Rightists) (Guomindang-Guomingemingjun Di San Jun (Youpai))\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\n$YUN_NRA_intro$\n\nThe Third Army is the successor of a few earlier armies aligned with the southern government including the Second National Protection Army and the First National Construction Army. It participated in a mutiny against the Kuomintang after Sun's death in 1925, only to be utterly routed.\n\nIt was then reorganised as the Third Army under Zhu Peide, a Yunnan Kuomintang loyalist. It fought with distinction in the Eastern front of the Northern Expedition against Sun Chuanfang, but was ultimately forced to retreat with the rest of the NRA during the Long March. In Guizhou, the Third Army absorbed smaller Yunnan based military forces under Fan Shisheng and Jin Handing after the Kuomintang reorganised in Guizhou.\n\nThe Third Army's right is led by Zhu Peide, but his leadership is far from uncontested within their ranks. With a relatively regional focused agenda, he is not seen as a major threat by larger party forces.§!\n
KMT-MCC
Kuomintang - Moscow Committee Cliques (Guomindang-Mosike Pai)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nSun Yat-sen's successor as Generalissimo of the Guangzhou Military Government was Hu Hanmin, who was quickly sidelined by an alliance between Wang Jingwei, Chiang Kai-shek, and various other powerholders. The growing power of the left and the Chinese Syndicalist Party led to right wing figures within the Kuomintang to beg Hu Hanmin to stand up against them, something that came to pass in the inconclusive Fourth Plenum. Chiang sided against Hu, resulting in his allies' purge or exile.\n\nBefore the Northern Expedition, Hu and other rightist figures aligned with him formed a rival central committee in exile, ultimately finding a home in Moscow. Their return has given them some agency over the party Hu once ruled, but they resent their declining power in favour of their rivals within the party.§!\n
Old Dian Clique
Old Dian Clique Remnants (Remnants) (Jiu Dian Xì Junfa (Canbu))\n§LIn the aftermath of the Xinhai Revolution, the military came to dominate the politics of Yunnan. Initially led by Cai E, Tang Jiyao would succeed him following the former's ousting by Yuan Shikai due to his support for Song Jiaoren. Tang ceded power to Cai after he made his escape in the midst of Yuan Shikai's monarchical restoration and aided him in leading the National Protection Alliance, but became governor again following Cai's passing.\n\nAlthough a committed democrat and federalist, Tang Jiyao learned from the experiences of the National Protection War the valuable lesson that the military has the right to intervene in civilian politics. Hu Ruoyu has taken these lessons to heart, restoring order after Yunnan fell to chaos following the end of the Qing hegemony and return of political instability in Kunming.\n\nHu Ruoyu's new government is largely enforced by the military alone, though the gentry cooperates with the Kunming Administration in the name of law and order. While Hu Ruoyu may be decried as a tyrant by liberal and socialist agitators, his supporters see him as a bulwark against chaos and radicalism.§!\n
KMT-CCC
Kuomintang - CC Clique (Guomindang-CC Xi)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\nDuring the Xinhai Revolution, Chen Qimei led a branch of the Tongmenghui operating out of Shanghai that coordinated revolutionary activities in the Jiangnan region. Chen partnered with his fellow Zhejiang cadres Chiang Kai-shek and Dai Jitao, along with his nephew Chen Guofu to raise money and soldiers for the revolution. Operating an illegal stock exchange and coordinating activities with nationalistic triads, he was ultimately assassinated, likely on the orders of Zhang Zongchang under the orders of Yuan Shikai. Chiang met a similar fate after a bout in leadership of the Kuomintang about a decade later. Dai Jitao, the intellectual of the group, has retreated to their old bases after the Northern Expedition and worked to rebuild their intelligence network.\n\nThis tight network of political operatives evolved into a shadowy cabal known to outsiders as the CC Clique. Chen Guofu's younger brother, Chen Lifu has joined them as a prominent spokesman for this party faction, which dominates education, propaganda, and even intelligence gathering.§!\n
KMT-WPC
Kuomintang - Whampoa Clique (Mainline Faction) (Guomíndang-Huangbu Xi (Benliu))\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\n$YUN_NRA_intro$\n\nHe Yingqin was a leading instructor in Whampoa and Chiang's number one deputy within the First Army. A revolutionary from Guizhou, despite a major public falling out with Chiang he has managed to leverage his familiarity with the province during the NRA's exile period to build a collection of loyalists, friends, and protégés within the army that has become his powerbase. A conservative military man and not much of a thinker, he nevertheless offers a degree of stability that the party would otherwise lack.§!\n
KMT-NRA
Kuomintang - National Revolutionary Army (Remnants) (Guomindang-Guomingemingjun (Canbu))\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\n$YUN_NRA_intro$\n\nAfter the failure of the Northern Expedition, the right wing of the National Revolutionary Army was forced into a fighting retreat known as the Long March. The exhausted remnants of the 1st, 2nd, 3rd, 6th, and 7th Armies made it to their bases in Guizhou, where they consolidated under a five man junta with Zhu Peide nominally at its head. Distracted by conflicts in the East, these forces managed to survive the ensuing few years despite growing attrition and declining morale. Those who remain in Guizhou are extremely radicalised and vengeful.§!\n
KMT-WPC (Extremists)
Kuomintang - Whampoa Clique (Extremist Faction) (Guomindang-Huangbu Xi (Jíduan pai))\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\n$YUN_NRA_intro$\n\nThe Sun Yat-sen Society in Whampoa was an early anti-syndicalist radical group which traded insults and punches with leftists on campus. Further radicalised by the supposed leftist betrayal during the Northern Expedition as well as the intervention by foreign powers, many Whampoa alumni have grown radicalised during the exile period. They look to solutions in their own ultra-nationalism and Whampoa traditions as well as influence from foreign national populist groups like in Russia and Romania for how to save their nation from weakness and degeneracy.§!\n
KMT-BSS
Kuomintang - Blue Shirts Society (Guomindang-Lanyishe)\n§L$YUN_KMT_intro$\n\n$YUN_NRA_intro$\n\nThe Sun Yat-sen Society in Whampoa was an early anti-syndicalist radical group which traded insults and punches with leftists on campus. Further radicalised by the supposed leftist betrayal during the Northern Expedition as well as the intervention by foreign powers, many Whampoa alumni have grown radicalised during the exile period. They look to solutions in their own ultra-nationalism and Whampoa traditions as well as influence from foreign national populist groups like in Russia and Romania for how to save their nation from weakness and degeneracy.\n\nOrganised by figures such as Teng Jie, the Blue Shirts Society has emerged from this militant nationalism as a secret society within the NRA dedicated to building a national populist state in China. Fanatical in nature, some have questioned their continued loyalty to General He Yingqin and even the party itself.§!\n
The Grand Republican Alliance is a quasi-legal political coalition of largely Southern Chinese parties operating in opposition towards the established Beiyang political order. Formed in 1931 after the swelling of anti-concessionist energy and nationalist agitation following the failure of the Zhili-Fengtian negotiation discussions, the Grand Republican Alliance would briefly ally with the retired Duan Qirui, and be joined by other \
In the aftermath of the Xinhai Revolution, the military came to dominate the politics of Yunnan. Initially led by Cai E, it was then taken over by Tang Jiyao who succeeded him following his ousting by Yuan Shikai due to his support for Song Jiaoren. Tang then ceded power back to Cai after he made his escape in the midst of Yuan Shikai's monarchical restoration and aided him in leading the National Protection Alliance. He then became governor again following Cai's passing.
Republicans
Independent Republicans and Intellectuals\n§LIn the aftermath of the 1932 Shanghai Uprising and electoral suspension, many liberal intellectuals fled the increasingly autocratic Zhili regime in favour of Southern China's federalist governments. In Yunnan, many educators found their way home, declaring their disgust for the Beijing Government and joined the burgeoning Federation of Democratic Chinese Parties (FCDP).\n\nWith Governor Tang's funding, they have enjoyed a certain degree of influence in the Kunming Administration. Among the gathering of progressive intellectuals within Yunnan, Su Honggang and Cun Shusheng have risen particularly high, forming their own intra-party groups within Kunming circles. Based in the National Southwestern Associated University, Su and Cun work with Crescent Moon Society members Liang Shiqiu and Wen Yiduo to promote democracy in Yunnan.§!\n

CMS
Crescent Moon Society (Xin Yue She)\n§LOriginally formed by Xu Zhimo in 1923 Shanghai as a bourgeois social club about art and drama, the Crescent Moon Society would evolve and rebrand itself as a politically inclined social club. Although many intellectuals came and went, including the likes of Hu Shih, the CMS would begin to revolve around Luo Longji, Liang Shiqiu, and Wen Yiduo as its intellectual core.\n\nIncreasingly harassed by League policemen following the Shanghai Uprising of 1932, the CMS leadership decided to move to Yunnan under the protection of Governor Tang Jiyao. Opening the National Southwestern Associated University as a refuge for fleeing league intellectuals, Luo and the CMS have continued to wage war on tyranny through words and free discussion. Although only one intellectual grouping among the many who have fled Sun's League, the CMS has risen above them all as one of the largest and most popular intellectual organisation in Yunnan Province.§!\n

Chamber of Commerce
Yunnan General Chamber of Commerce (Dian Zong Shanghui)\n§LAn organisation developed by Yunnan's powerful gentry class, the Chamber of Commerce is dedicated towards preserving their business interests. Originally gaining influence in the aftermath of Yunnan's devastation during the 1800s, the gentry have stifled radical reforms in the province, like containing Viceroy Li Jingxi's reforms to Kunming alone.\n\nDuring the Warlord Era, Cai E and Tang Jiyao have worked with them to ensure that some reforms in the province can be undertaken without gentry resistance. The gentry have come to dominate various local assemblies and control much of Yunnan's industry. In recent times, the Chamber of Commerce has come to be led by Miao Yuntai, an enterprising bureaucrat leading economic reform in the Yunnan Provincial Administration.§!\n
GRA-PGP
$UPC_PGP_exiled_party_long_tt$\n§L$YUN_GRA_intro$\n\nFormed as a union between Zhang Taiyan's Society for Promoting the Self-Rule Movement and Tang Jiyao's Democratic Society, the People's Government Party operates as Tang Jiyao's personal party, promoting his ideas of Provincial Autonomy, Anti-militarism, and People's Government. However, the party is not solely his, as Zhang Taiyan continues to retain a large following. Zhang's wing of the party promotes a more bottom-up variant of federalism and the vesting of power into local communities.\n\nThe People's Government Party received a boon from the Shanghai Uprising of 1932 and the subsequent Zhili crackdowns, as many intellectuals fled south to join up with his Federalist regime. Forming an alliance with the progressive intellectuals of the new National Southwestern Associated University, the People's Government Party emerged as the civilian arm of Tang Jiyao's government.\n\nCDL led protests against Tang Jiyao's authoritarianism dealt a nearly fatal blow to his democratic image, and Tang was toppled in a coup shortly afterwards. His son, Tang Xiaoying, has fled to exile in Guangzhou where he has attempted to rally supporters and build stronger ties to the broader GRA. Seen as more liberal than his father, Tang Xiaoying may still have an opportunity yet to return to power.§!\n
Grand Republican Alliance - People's Government Party (Gonghe Datongmeng RenMin ZhengFu Dang)
GRA-PGP

However, the party is not solely his, as Zhang Taiyan continues to retain a large following. Zhang's wing of the party promotes a more bottom-up variant of federalism and the vesting of power into local communities.\n\nThe People's Government Party received a boon from the Shanghai Uprising of 1932 and the subsequent Zhili crackdowns, as many intellectuals fled south to join up with his Federalist regime. Forming an alliance with the progressive intellectuals of the new National Southwestern Associated University, Tang's People's Government Party has emerged as a genuine democratic party able to stand up to Zhili oppressors in Beijing and their provincial proxies in neighbouring provinces. The civilian side of Tang's government apparatus, the PGP is and will continue to be a key component of Tang's government.§!\n
Grand Republican Alliance - People's Government Party (Gonghe Datongmeng RenMin ZhengFu Dang)
GRA-PGP
$UPC_PGP_party_long_tt$\n§L$YUN_GRA_intro$\n\nFormed as a union between Zhang Taiyan's Society for Promoting the Self-Rule Movement and Tang Jiyao's Democratic Society, the People's Government Party was shattered by Tang Jiyao's overthrow and death. Sympathetic intellectuals, writers, and propagandists have either fled to greener pastures or face censorship by the new regime, Zhang Taiyan has retreated into seclusion, and the new chairman Tang Xiaoying (Tang Jiyao's son) seems more interested in the Young China Party than managing the decrepit ruins of Tang's movement. Nevertheless, Tang Jiyao's influence continues to be felt in Yunnan as many of his old retainers hang onto to various jobs in the administration.§!\n
Tang Clique
Tang Jiyao's Clique (Tang Pai)\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nAlthough a committed democrat and federalist, Tang Jiyao learned from the experiences of the National Protection War the valuable lesson that the military has the right to intervene in civilian politics. In the halls of Tang's government, his military wing continues to profess the ideas of Cai E, in that those in the military possessed a more highly developed understanding of the nation's needs rather than the common people, that the professional soldier was deemed to have superior competence in all matters of the nation-state.\n\nGovernor Tang believes all this, but he also knows that a slide back to autocracy would go against the evolution of the Chinese nation, and balances his military camp with the interests of his political party, the People's Government Party. Tang's government maintains a vast coalition of idealistic democrats, ambitious and heavy handed generals, and capable bureaucrats working together uneasily.§!\n
Dian Clique
Dian Clique (Dian Pai)\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nTang built up a powerful governing apparatus during his decades in power while in Yunnan, combining a powerful military, a functioning civilian bureaucracy, ties with the gentry and merchant elite, and an ideological platform built around a conservative, nationalistic brand of Federalism. As that mighty machine grew from a regional force to a national one, the divisions between the smaller cliques in Yunnan blurred until they became functionally irrelevant for most outsiders. Yunnanese figures control many levers of power in the new republic, much to the chagrin of others.§!\n
Long Clique
Long Yun's Clique (Long Pai)\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nAlthough a committed democrat and federalist, Tang Jiyao learned from the experiences of the National Protection War the valuable lesson that the military has the right to intervene in civilian politics. However, Tang Jiyao would continue to maintain a balance between his military forces, liberal allies, and bureaucrats aligned with gentry interests.\n\nAlthough Long Yun's rise was far from orderly, he has kept much of the government apparatus of the Tang administration in place. From Li Jingxi to Cai E to Tang Jiyao to Long Yun, the current administration but the current in a long line of reformers seeking to improve and better Yunnan Province, and perhaps provide an example for the rest of the nation to follow.§!\n
Long Yun's Clique (Long Pai)\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nAlthough a committed democrat and federalist, Tang Jiyao learned from the experiences of the National Protection War the valuable lesson that the military has the right to intervene in civilian politics. However, Tang Jiyao would continue to maintain a balance between his military forces, liberal allies, and bureaucrats aligned with gentry interests.\n\nAlthough Long Yun's rise was far from orderly, he has kept much of the government apparatus of the Tang administration in place. From Li Jingxi to Cai E to Tang Jiyao to Long Yun, the current administration but the current in a long line of reformers seeking to improve and better Yunnan Province.\n\nUnexpectedly, their successful leadership brought them from a minor regional faction to the grand unifiers of all of China as the head of the National Protection Alliance. Now, Long rules with an iron fist, balancing the lessons of all of his mentors as he navigates a new era in China.§!\n
Lu Clique
Lu Han's Clique (Lu Pai)\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nLu Han was a close childhood friend of Long Yun, but turned on him as Long began to concentrate power around himself at the expense of his former loyalists. This led to many of his senior generals switching sides and aiding in a coup against him. Afterwards many of Long's former supporters (at least in the military) turned to Lu Han as their new leader. Lu, an ambitious and flexible warlord, has staked his claim to leadership on a vague sense of populism and nationalism.§!\n
Garrison Commanders
Provincial Garrison Commanders (Sheng Zhujun Zhihui Guan)\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nAlthough a committed democrat and federalist, Tang Jiyao has learned from the experiences of the National Protection War, Warlord Era, and ensuing decade of violence and chaos that one thing is important above all else: Keep your House in order.\n\nBuilt upon the rather fragile house of cards of the 1920s, the Yunnan Clique has been fraught with infighting. First it was Gu Pinzhen, then Long Yun, Hu Ruoyu, Li Xuanting, and Zhang Ruji. Both made their gambits to oust the King of Yunnan, and during his lost ordeal, Tang Jiyao only narrowly escaped deposition. Now with Sun Du as Garrison Commander in the West, and Tang centred around Kunming itself, an uneasy peace has endured for years with Long Yun in the North, and Hu, Li, and Zhang in the south. Whilst ostensibly loyal, the Mengzi and Long Yun Cliques's true intentions remain to be seen.§!\n
Mengzi Clique
$YUN_hu_ruoyu_clique_party_long_tt$\n§L$YUN_NPA_intro$\n\nAlthough a committed democrat and federalist, Tang Jiyao learned from the experiences of the National Protection War the valuable lesson that the military has the right to intervene in civilian politics. Hu Ruoyu has taken these lessons to heart, restoring order after Yunnan fell to chaos following the end of the Qing hegemony and return of political instability in Kunming.\n\nHu Ruoyu's new government is largely enforced by the military alone, though the gentry cooperates with the Kunming Administration in the name of law and order. While Hu Ruoyu may be decried as a tyrant by liberal and socialist agitators, his supporters see him as a bulwark against chaos and radicalism.§!\n

He also managed to do the impossible - unite China under his banner. Now he is expected to rule in a manner similar to the Zhili before him, indeed he has worked to absorb man ex-Zhili politicians to build a civilian facade while a junta of his generals decide national affairs behind closed doors.§!\n

Wang Fusheng
Participating in a standard education in Western Yunnan, Wang Fusheng would leave his interior province to be admitted to the liberal arts prep class of Beijing University in 1918, and in 1920 he would join the French Literature department. During his time in Beijing, Wang began to flirt with the allure of Syndicalism, becoming into contact with syndicalist theorists such as Deng Zhongxia, Li Dazhao and others. That same year under Li Dazhao's guidance alongside 19 others, Wang would help initiate China's First Syndicalist research group — the Beijing University Syndicalist Theory Research Society. Serving as head of the French translation group, Wang would translate a flurry of revolutionary theories emerging from France following its syndicalist revolution. Joining the Beijing Socialist Youth League founded by Li Dazhao, Wang would eventually be admitted as a member of the Chinese Syndicalist Party in 1921.\n\nLater teaching in Shaanxi province due to poor finances, Wang would endeavour to continuously spread syndicalist ideas and organise on behalf of the CSP. Returning to Beijing University to resume his studies, he and his brother would initiate the New Yunnan Society, publishing a weekly \

Li Xin
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 12th, 1897, in Longling County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §rYunnan Syndicalist Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a poor peasant family in rural Yunnan, Li Xin and a few of his friends would trek for more than a month to finally arrive in Kunming, intending to be admitted to the provincial middle school. Becoming influenced by revolutionary and progressive ideals, Li Xin would become committed to attempting to eradicate inequality in China. Graduating in 1919, Li would be admitted to the Department of Agriculture of the Southeast University in Nanjing. Transferring to the Horticulture Department of Beijing Agricultural University, Li Xin would be influenced by the ideas of Syndicalism, realising that only through revolution could oppression and exploitation be eliminated.\n\nIn 1925 Li Xin would join the Syndicalist Party of China, participating in the formation of the New Yunnan Society with Wang Desan and Wang Fusheng, and the establishment of the \
Zhu De
Born to a Hakka tenant farmer family in Sichuan, Zhu De would do odd jobs and participate in the Gelaohui secret society, studying the Taiping Heavenly Rebellion and its effects on China. As he prepared to enter the civil service, Zhu had as one of his tutors a devout Kang Youwei supporter, who led him to fall under the allure of revolutionary sentiment. Passing the district and prefectural exams only to see the abolition of the examination system in 1905, the already disillusioned with tradition Zhu decided to enter Kunming Military University. Attracted to the new militarism, he enlisted in the Kunming Military Academy as one of the few Sichuanese students accepted.\n\nGraduating from a special accelerated class after participating in the Double Ninth Uprising, Zhu De increasingly became one of the protégés of Cai E. Serving as a military instructor, Zhu fought in Cai E's First Army during the National Protection War, and later in the Constitutional Protection War. Conspiring with Gu Pinzhen to overthrow Tang Jiyao, Gu then attempted to embezzle funds to finance a trip to Europe. With Tang Jiyao's resurgence, Zhu had to flee to Shanghai, and with the funding from Jin Handing, started travelling to Europe with Sun Bingwen.\n\nStudying in Paris, Zhu would meet Zhou Enlai, Chen Yi and Li Lisan, formally, albeit secretly, joining the Chinese Syndicalist Party in 1922. Later studying in Germany, he became enamoured by European military theory. Returning to China to participate in the Northern Expedition, he attempted to mobilise Yang Sen to join the revolutionary cause, to no avail. Establishing the NRA 3rd Army Officer Training Corps, Zhu Peide followed the rest of the 3rd Army into Guizhou. Considering a famed Yunnan political heavyweight, Zhu De spent the rest of the interwar drafting military theories, carving his group of leftist officers and clashing doctrinally with Bai Chongxi.

§YBorn:§! §LDecember 1st, 1886, in Yilong County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RThird Army Leftists§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$YUN_zhu_de_bio$§!
Chen Yi
§YBorn:§! §LAugust 26th, 1901, in Lezhi County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RThird Army Leftists§!\n§YMilitary Career:§! §LBorn to a minor landlord family in Sichuan, Chen Yi attended the Chengdu Institute of Technology at the age of 15. Chen's life trajectory was changed decisively when he moved to Paris in 1919 for a work study programme. It was there that Chen met Zhou Enlai and Cai Hesen, and was exposed to Marxist ideas. Upon returning to China, Cai brought Chen into the Chinese Syndicalist Party as a member of its youth league.\n\nIn 1923, he met Yan Changyi and Xiao Zhensheng at the University of China and France in Beijing, becoming secretary of the Chinese Syndicalist Party's branch at that institution. In 1924, Chen joined the Literacy Research Association led by Mao Dun, and was elected as president of the school union of his university. Following the First Reorganisation of the Kuomintang and establishment of the Chinese United Front, Chen became secretary of the CSP League of the Beijing Student Federation and worked closely with the local KMT branch.\n\nAfter the Dagukuo incident where Japanese warships bombarded the Taku Forts in support of the Fengtian Clique and Guominjun responded by laying naval mines, Chen took part in the great protest against the Ultimatum of Eight-Power on March 18th 1926, where the powers demanded Chinese warlords demilitarise the port according to the Boxer Protocol, and he survived the subsequent governmental crackdown which resulted in over 40 students and citizens being killed, known as the March 18th Massacre. After being appointed Secretary of the Northern District Committee of the Chinese Syndicalist Party, Chen returned to Sichuan to serve in a military role in the upcoming Chinese revolution under Zhu De. However, fate did not favour the revolutionaries, with German intervention bringing the national revolution crumbling down like a house of cards. Chen evacuated to Guizhou under Zhu De in the 3rd Army during the chaos. Despite the setbacks suffered by the KMT, Chen remains confident that the socialist revolution will come about in China, one way or another.§!

Tang Huaiyuan
§YBorn:§! §L1886, in Jiangchuan County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §RThird Army Leftists§!\n§YBackground:§! §LLosing his father at a young age would un-phase Tang Huaiyuan, who would go onto pass the provincial examination in 1909, being admitted to Kunming Military Academy. Classmates with the likes of Zhu De and Jin Handing, he would become close blood brothers with the two of them. Influenced by the revolutionary ideals circulated at the behest of Li Genyuan in Kunming, Tang would join the Tongmenghui in 1910. Participating in the Yunnan adjacent uprising to Xinhai, the Double Ninth Uprising (Ninth day of the Ninth lunar month), Tang was selected as one of 100 outstanding students to form a special class alongside the likes of Zhu Peide, Zhu De and Jin to receive unique training and be promoted to platoon leaders that same year.\n\nServing under Cai E in the National Protection War, Tang would display meritorious performance in battle, being rapidly promoted to brigade commander by 1918. Following internal Yunnan Army infighting, Tang Huaiyuan would support Gu Pinzhen's bid to oust Tang Jiyao, later fleeing upon Tang Jiyao's return in 1922. Living in Shanghai with Zhu and Jin, they would meet Dr. Sun in Guangdong, with Zhu departing to Europe to study through Jin's financing.\n\nJoining the 3rd Army of the National Revolutionary Army, Tang would teach at an officer's school, before being forced to retreat as the Northern Expedition collapsed. Uncomfortably close to Tang Jiyao yet again, Tang Huaiyuan and Jin Handing would sync up with Zhu De yet again after his return from Europe, with Tang becoming a core member of Zhu De's informal grouping within the 3rd Army.§!
Chen Cheng
§YBorn:§! January 4th, 1898, in Qingtian County, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing\n§YBackground:§! §LAn ambitious, prestigious, some would describe arrogant, stalwart of the Kuomintang, Chen Cheng's life is colourful and experienced. Forcing himself through education despite his circumstances, he would be thrust into the world of the military through his application to Baoding Military Academy in his youth.\n\nBriefly moonlighting in the Guangdong Army in 1920, Chen joined the Kuomintang, and then returned to Baoding to finish his studies. Graduating in 1922, he was recruited by his mentor Deng Yanda to serve as his lieutenant adjutant. Infamously shot whilst protecting Dr. Sun, Chen would land himself in the purview of Chiang Kai-shek. Following the establishment of Whampoa, Sun, Chiang and Deng all vouched for Chen's enlistment there.\n\nAs a student, instructor, and team captain, Chen saw distinction in the National Revolutionary Army's exploits of the 1920s. Yet without Chiang or Deng, Chen would see himself sidelined by He Yingqin. Now superseding the old Generalissimo, Chen's wide understanding of land reform and his pseudo-socialist credentials have, quite peculiarly, turned the New Right leftward.§!\n\n§YNotes: He is noted to live a particularly spartan lifestyle, deprived of pleasures. Similarly, he is devoutly against corruption.§!

Luo Zhuoying
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 19th, 1896, in Dabu County, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SCivil Engineering Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LA native Hakka, Luo Zhuoying would undergo a standard education and later apply to Baoding Military Academy in 1918. Being admitted to the eighth artillery section of the academy, Luo would end up becoming best friends and blood brothers with Chen Cheng and Zhou Zhirou. Graduating in July 1922, Luo would return to his home-town to serve as an academic director and principal before being recommend by Kuomintang politician Zou Lu to serve as the major staff officer of the Chaomei Army, but Luo would resign immediately. Heavily recommend to join the recently founded Whampoa Military Academy by Chen Cheng, Luo would slip in at the tail end of 1924, beginning a relationship wherein wherever Chen Cheng rose in prominence, Luo Zhuoying was sure to follow close behind.\n\nServing as Chen Cheng's direct subordinate during the Eastern Expedition, Luo's capacity to command artillery gained him great praise within the National Revolutionary Army. Upon the start of the Northern Expedition, Chen Cheng's artillery battalion fought under the command of 1st Army commander He Yingqin, marching into Fujian and Zhejiang. Briefly rerouted to relieve Guangzhou from German invasion, Chen and Luo's artillery did little to turn the tides, and following disastrous infighting, the assassination of Chiang Kai-shek, and the chaotic retreat to Guizhou, Chen Cheng would be shifted to the political department by He Yingqin, whilst Luo replaced him as commander of the 1st Army's artillery.\n\nA remarkable strategist and tactician, Luo would work in tandem with Chen Cheng's administrative capacity to create the Civil Engineering Clique within the NRA.§!\n\n§YNotes: Best friends and his right hand man, Luo Zhuoying is known as the \

Determined to join the Army, Hu Lian would enter the military profession as a clerk under a subordinate of Hu Jingyi. Yet soon after Hu would receive a letter from a relative in Guangzhou, urging him to join the Whampoa Military Academy. Wei Lihuang
§YBorn:§! §LFebruary 16th, 1897, in Hefei County, Anhui Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §SCivil Engineering Clique§!\n§YMilitary Career:§! §LImmersing himself in cultural classics at a young age, Wei Lihuang briefly served as a soldier in the local military during Xinhai, before serving as the head teacher of a military training class. Influenced by the revolutionary ideals of his elder brother, Wei Lihuang joined the mass armed revolt in Anhui during the Second Revolution. Seeing training in Hubei Army Cadet Camp, he eventually found himself in the Guangdong Army in 1915. Elected to serve as one of Dr. Sun Yat-sen's bodyguards in 1917, Wei further strengthened his understanding of the Three Principles, joining the KMT. Promoted due to his quick thinking in fighting forces of the Anhui clique, Wei would see victorious service in all of the nascent Kuomintang's military endeavours, serving dutifully under Xu Chongzhi.\n\nFighting in the Eastern Expeditions and the Merchant Corps Rebellion, Wei was eventually integrated into the 1st Army of the National Revolutionary Army in 1925. Under the command of He Yingqin in the Northern Expedition, Wei proved to be a brave, resolute, and expert soldier and commander, being rapidly promoted to Division Commander of the 14th Division. With the Northern Expedition floundering and Guangzhou captured, Wei Lihuang was one of the few NRA commanders to still exhibit constant military successes. Yet, he could not stem the advance of the Zhili. Following the 1st Army into a chaotic retreat into Guizhou, Wei was commonly utilised as a delaying force in order to allow weaker units to escape.\n\nEver at the mercy of his superior, Wei Lihuang would be employed as one of the most capable NRA commanders, warding off any encroachment into Guizhou, either from Old Guizhou or Old Guangxi. Disagreeing with He Yingqin's management of the Whampoa Cliques, and in staunch opposition to Teng Jie's Blue Shirts, Wei Lihuang found himself seeing eye-to-eye with Chen Cheng and his Civil Engineering Clique, becoming a half-hearted member.§!\n\n§YNotes: Considered a military genius by many, rivalling that of Bai Chongxi, Wei Lihuang has gained the moniker of the \
Zhang Qun
Attending the Baoding National Army Crash Course in his early years, in 1908 Zhang Qun would find himself sent to Japan to study at the Shinbu Gakko, wherein upon a chance arrangement he became a close friend and classmate of the prodigy Chiang Kai-shek. That same year, Zhang was swept up in the revolutionary current of China, joining the Tongmenghui. Following the outbreak of Xinhai, Zhang joined his friend in fighting under the command of Chen Qimei, ultimately serving as staff officer of Chiang's division. Forever tying their fates together with him, Zhang Qun fought with Chiang in the Second Revolution in 1913, and after serving as a staff officer in 1915 for Zhejiang Province, he was recruited by Cen Chunxuan.\n\nHe ended up in Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Canton Government in 1917, ultimately fighting in his failed revolution before returning home to be employed by Xiong Kewu as director of Sichuan Police Department. After Xiong's defeat in 1923, Zhang was once again recruited by Chiang to serve as his staff officer, in 1926. Serving as general councillor and member of the Military Committee, Zhang Qun would have a muted role in intra National Revolutionary Army squabbles. Following the Northern Expedition's collapse and the death of his friend, Zhang Qun had little time to mourn as he followed the \
§YBorn:§! May 9th, 1889, in Huayang County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing\n§YBackground:§! §L$YUN_zhang_qun_bio$§!
§YBorn:§! §LMay 9th, 1889, in Huayang County, Sichuan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §m(New) Political Science Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §L$YUN_zhang_qun_bio$§!
Yang Yongtai
§YBorn:§! §L1880, in Gaozhou, Guangdong Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §m(New) Political Science Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBorn to a wealthy family in urban Guangdong, Yang Yongtai would receive a strict traditional education in his early years, passing the examination to be come a Qing Scholar in 1897. At the age of 21, Yang would find himself at Guangzhou Higher School receiving a Western styled education, later transferring to Beijing School of Political Science and Law to study. Returning home after graduation, Yang would become something of a local celebrity, known for his fluent writing, quick thinking, profound arguments and active ideas. As his renown grew, so too did his desire for revolutionary change, drafting a series of articles expressing his advocacy for constitutional monarchy.\n\nElected to the Provisional National Assembly in 1912, Yang would find himself out of a job due to Yuan Shikai's machinations, and would end up in contact with Huang Xing and Dr. Sun Yat-sen. Devoting himself to Sun's Chinese Revolutionary Party, Yang Yongtai would serve in the National Protection War, and would end up in the staff of Li Liejun, appointed as director of the Finance Bureau. Becoming a founding member of the Political Science Society alongside the likes of Li Genyuan, Yang would be appointed Director of Finance in Dr. Sun's 1917 Canton Government, but due to influence from Political Science, he would refuse the position. Following the machinations of Tang Jiyao and Political Science, Sun would resign in anger, and Yang Yongtai would find himself Governor of Guangdong in 1920.\n\nFearful of retribution, Yang would flee to the Beiyang Government, and following Cao Kun's bribery, Yang would end up in Shanghai, where he would remain until 1927. Following Chiang Kai-shek stepping down that year, Yang would draft a flurry of letters to various Kuomintang officials expressing both his desire to re-enter politics and see Chiang restored. Ignored by most, Yang would use his connections to find himself under Wang Boqun's employ. Noticing his ambition following the retreat to Guizhou, Zhang Qun would pull strings to see Yang Yongtai rise to prominence once more. Considered Zhang's deputy, Yang's affirmation of his leadership has brought the Old and New Political Science Cliques together.§!

He went on to study mineralogy in Yale University, receiving a master's degree in physics and chemistry.\n\nWhen the 1911 Xinhai Revolution kicked off, Kong Xiangxi led local students and business groups in Taigu to maintain order. While in Japan raising funds for Sun Yet-sen's Chinese Revolutionary Party, he met Sun's English secretary Song Ailing, the eldest sibling of the Song family. The two married in 1914, and returned back to China to do business in Shanxi. His work in education and business caught the attention of Shanxi's governor Yan Xishan, who hired him as a councilor. While working for Yan Xishan, Kong Xiangxi helped promote Shanxi's image as the \
Li Genyuan
§YBorn:§! §LJune 6th, 1879, in Tengyue County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §m(New) Political Science Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LStudying traditional Chinese culture in his youth, Li became increasingly dejected with the weakness and frailty of Chinese society. Taking the affairs of China upon himself, Li Genyuan would harbour strong anti-Qing sentiments from his early 20s. Admitted to the Japanese Shikan Gakko in 1904, Li attended the founding meeting of the Tongmenghui in Tokyo, building at the same time a strong bond with the likes of Cai E and Tang Jiyao. He returned to Yunnan in 1909, being appointed deputy commandant of the Kunming Military Course, a mystifying prospect for the young Li.\n\nSubmitting an additional list of his fellow Shikan Gakko graduates to be transferred to Yunnan, Li transformed the Military Course into the modern Kunming Academy, becoming its first Principal. Turning it into a hotbed of revolutionary sentiment, Li Genyuan would promote the Three Principles to his students, request Li Liejun to serve as a tutor, and eventually conspired with Cai E to launch the Double Ninth Uprising in tandem with Xinhai. Serving in various capacities at the whim of Cai, Li Genyuan was seen as Cai E's only potential equal in Yunnan, and yet he would be whisked away in 1913 to serve in the Beiyang House of Representatives. Almost immediately marked for death by Yuan Shikai, Li had to flee into the arms of Cen Chunxuan, Dr. Sun and Huang Xing.\n\nArranging for Cai E to return to Kunming in 1915, Li eventually became governor of Shaanxi in 1917, later becoming Commander of the Yunnan Army stationed in Guangdong. Opposing Cao Kun's bribery in 1923, Li resigned from the Beiyang Government, opting for a life of reflection and retirement with his family. Returning to the limelight after a decade of retirement, Li Genyuan's credentials have garnered him much respect, and animosity, from many within Yunnan.§!\n\n§YNotes: He is the last of a dying breed of revolutionary, yet forever holds true to his motto: \

He returned to Yunnan in 1909, being appointed deputy commandant of the Kunming Military Course.\n\nSubmitting an additional list of his fellow Shikan Gakko graduates to be transferred to Yunnan, Li transformed the Military Course into the modern Kunming Academy, becoming its first Principal. Turning it into a hotbed of revolutionary sentiment, Li would promote the Three Principles to his students, request Li Liejun to serve as a tutor, and eventually conspired with Cai E to launch the Double Ninth Uprising in tandem with Xinhai. After graduation in 1915, Xiong would serve in the Yunnan Army under the auspices of Li Liejun, serving in both the National Protection War and the 1917 Revolution. In 1921, Xiong was recommended by the General Staff of the Guangdong Military Government to study at the Shikan Gakko, and after graduating in 1924, he would return to China to serve as director of education at the Guangzhou Yunnan Army Military Academy and later party representative of the National Revolutionary Army's First Division. Still serving as its party representative as it was expanded into the 14th Army, Xiong would see field service as commander of the 1st Division.\n\nFollowing the Northern Expedition's failure, Xiong would luckily escape with the remnants of his Fourteenth Army fellows to Guizhou, where he would swiftly attach himself to Zhang Qun's various administrative posts. Gu Zhenglun
§YBorn:§! §LSeptember 23rd, 1890, in Anshun, Guizhou Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §LIndependent§!\n§YBackground:§! §LThe elder sibling of the Gu brothers, Gu Zhenglun chose a career in the military from a young age. In 1906, Gu graduated from the Guizhou Army Primary School and continued to the Hubei Army Middle School. In 1909, Gu was selected to study abroad in Japan's Tokyo Shinbu Gakko, specially made for Chinese students. During his time in Japan, Gu came to sympathise with the underground republican nationalist movement, the Tongmenghui. Gu further committed himself to the nationalist cause by taking part in the Xinhai Revolution of 1911.\n\nAfter finishing his studies in Japan, Gu returned home to Guizhou where he served as part of the local military. When Sun Yat-sen kicked off the Constitutional Protection Movement, Gu once again aligned with Sun and marched into Sichuan. When the Old Guangxi Clique betrayed the Guangzhou Nationalist Government, Gu mobilised his forces against Lu Rongting's renegade province and occupied Guilin. Gu Zhenglun served ably in the Northern Expedition, but German intervention halted Kuomintang ambitions in China, and caused him to flee with the rest of the NRA to Guizhou.\n\nUtilising his connections and credentials within Guizhou province, Gu Zhenglun managed to position himself as an influential figure in Guizhou provincial politics. Maintaining connections with Paris through his brothers and colluding with generals Zhu Peide and He Yingqin against Tang Jiyao, Gu serves as a bridge between Wang Jingwei's Central Committee and the KMT remnants in Yunnan. Yet not aligned to any faction in the KMT diaspora within Guizhou, many see Gu as an additional pawn in the game between the various NRA armies, the PSC and the CC Clique.§!

Jin Handing
§YBorn:§! §L1891, in Jiangchuan County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cThird Army Rightists§!\n§YBackground:§! §LWith a revolutionary desire at a young age, Jin Handing was admitted to the Kunming Military Academy in 1909, becoming friends with the likes of Zhu Peide and Zhu De. Participating in the Double Ninth Uprising, Jin would later participate in the National Protection War, serving under Cai E's First Army. Building a strong friendship with Zhu De along the way, Jin Handing weathered the various Yunnan power struggles with him at his side. Becoming acting commander-in-chief following Gu Pinzhen's power play in 1921, he had to flee following Tang Jiyao's return, exiling himself to Shanghai. Financing Zhu De's studies in Europe, Jin resided in Hong Kong until 1926, when he sprang into action for another chance to serve the nation.\n\nRecruiting more than 2,000 troops, he saw his men organised into the 16th Division of the National Revolutionary Army, aiding in capturing Nanchang. With his troops expanded into the 9th Army of the NRA, Jin's elevation to army commander was short lived, as due to the German intervention and Kuomintang infighting, the Northern Expedition soon floundered and collapsed. This resulted in Jin Handing having to lead his now shattered 9th Army into the Guizhou-Guangxi region.\n\nOnce again meeting with Zhu De upon his return to China, the two would discuss menial things like their past, or what Zhu De learnt whilst in Germany, or even his increasingly left-leaning revolutionary principles. Following the outbreak of Xinhai, Dai became connected with Chen Qimei whilst participating in the Shanghai Uprising, later leading to a position as Dr. Sun's personal secretary and Japanese translator. Chen Lifu
The younger brother of Chen Guofu and nephew to Chen Qimei, Chen Lifu attended Tianjin Beiyang University, studying engineering and mining. Upon graduation from Tianjin Beiyang University, Chen went to the United States to continue his studies, receiving a master's degree in metallurgy from the University of Pittsburgh. Unlike his brother Chen Guofu, uncle Chen Qimei, and close friend Chiang Kai-shek, Chen Lifu was uninterested in politics, but was convinced by Chiang and Chen Guofu to join the Guangzhou Nationalist Government which was seeking to unify China and purge the corrupt Beiyang warlords.\n\nWhen Chiang was killed and the Northern Expedition failed, Chen Lifu followed his brother into Shanghai where they hoped to consolidate their influence within the Kuomintang by continuing to operate investment interests and stock exchanges. While Chen Guofu established himself as a prominent figure in the Kuomintang's right wing Nationalist circles, Chen Lifu remained in the shadows, assisting his brother where he could, but also dedicating himself to the party's civil bureaucracy. With his engineering expertise, connections and propaganda know-how, he is considered a valuable asset to the party. However, simultaneously, this makes Chen Lifu quite the dangerous enemy, should you garner the ire of either Chen brother.\n\n§YNotes: A devoted practitioner of traditional Chinese medicine, Chen Lifu preaches an odd form of Dr. Sun's Three Principles, intermixed with his own vitalism ideology.§!

Chen Guofu
§YBorn:§! §LOctober 27th, 1892, in Wucheng County, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §aCCC§!\n§YBackground:§! §LChen Guofu spent his early life in the shadow of his famous uncle Chen Qimei, one of the founders of the Republic of China, ally of Sun Yat-sen, and mentor to Chiang Kai-shek. In 1920, Chen Guofu operated in the Shanghai Stock Exchange alongside Chiang in order to fund the Kuomintang. Chen Guofu found his fortunes increase with Chiang's elevation to Headmaster of Sun's Whampoa Military Academy, with Chen put in charge of military recruitment in Shanghai.\n\nWhen the Northern Expedition turned into a disaster and Chen's old friend Chiang was killed, he and his brother fled Guangzhou for Shanghai where some of the remnants of the Kuomintang had consolidated. Chen Guofu has become a prominent voice in the Kuomintang's right wing, staunchly opposing the Leftist Central Executive Committee's alliance with syndicalist forces. With Chen Guofu dominating the bureaucracy of the Right Wing of the Kuomintang, and his brother at his side, he will not see Sun Yat-sen's National Revolution fall to such darkness. No, he will reshape the National Revolution in honour of Chiang Kai-shek, Chen Qimei, and all Nationalist martyrs who have given their lives for China's future.§!\n\n§YNotes: Alongside his brother, Chen Guofu has continuously worked to monopolise his influence within the fragmented party, spreading the Central Club's tendrils wherever they can go.§!

Ouyang Ge

The Fujian naval cliques, constituting the majority, attempted to return back to the Beijing government under the auspices of Lin Baoyi, and tried to exclude non-Fujianese from serving in the navy.\n\nFollowing Ouyang Ge's reports of such events to Dr. Sun, Chen Ce and other non-Fujian naval admirals launched a suppression of all Fujian naval personnel in the Constitutional Protection Fleet, in which Ouyang participated, forever gaining Sun's trust. Destined to be a shining and brilliant soldier, He Yingqin initially attended a Wuchang Army School before being sent to study at the Tokyo Shinbu Gakko. Meeting Chiang Kai-shek during his time there, He started to be influenced by the Anti-Qing rhetoric of the Tongmenghui, which he would later join.\n\nFighting in the Xinhai Revolution, he then graduated in Japan in 1916, before returning to Guizhou to serve as a military instructor under Wang Wenhua. Seeing brutal service in the Northern Expedition, He once again found himself in his home province. Chiang's de facto successor in Whampoa, He had to contend with Generalissimo Zhu Peide. Following the establishment of Party control in Guangdong, He Yingqin successfully sidelined Zhu and negotiated a compromise with Hu Hanmin.\n\nNow at the helm of the revived Nationalist Government, He Yingqin wields a array of supporters, ranging from the revolutionary CC Clique to the nationalistic Blue Shirts Society. A humourless soldier thrust upon the centre stage, He Yingqin shall either fall like his old friend and be forgotten as time goes by, or adapt to his role as the heir of revolution and be remembered as China's saviour in its darkest hour.

Appointed lieutenant colonel adjutant of the staff department, Jiang Dingwen would become a colonel staff officer in 1922, at the mere age of 27. Serving in various staff roles, Jiang Dingwen would willingly give up his rank and position to enter Whampoa Academy, becoming captain of the second student team, and a military instructor.\n\nHaving the odd habit of waking up early, he would often be met by principal Chiang Kai-shek. Reportedly, upon a field exercise being held at Whampoa, a foreign advisor was observing the exercises with Chiang and Jiang in tow. Asking impromptue questions, Jiang Dingwen would answer fluently, to the amazement of the advisor. Participating in the suppression of the Guangzhou Merchant Rebellion, Jiang would also see service in the First Eastern Expedition, gaining Chiang's personal respect. Gui Yongqing
§YBorn:§! §LMarch 7th, 1901, in Guixi County, Jiangxi Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §PWhampoa Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LSelected along with fellow Guixi people to study in Japan at a young age, Gui Yongqing would ultimately return to China upon hearing of the founding of Whampoa Military Academy, joining its first class. Participating in the Eastern Expeditions against Chen Jiongming, Gui is notable as one of the few Whampoa soldiers to have actively participated in looting and pillaging, which was noticed by Li Zhilong. Upon hearing of this, Chiang Kai-shek was furious, ordering that Gui be executed to serve as a lesson to the rest of Whampoa, requesting that He Zhonghan be the executioner. Albeit due to Gui Yongqing's connections to He Zhonghan, the latter intervened on behalf of the former, petitioning He Yingqin to ask Chiang to spare his life, and grant him a more lenient punishment.\n\nServing as commander of the special forces battalion of the 1st Army of the NRA, he would enter Fujian in 1926 during the Northern Expedition, yet in the failure of the Battle of Longtan, Gui would ultimately be sidelined following his performance. Miraculously surviving the collapse of the Northern Expedition, Gui Yongqing would find himself within Guizhou, and within an army far more honourable than he is.\n\nDesperate for employment, Gui would utilise his experience in amphibious warfare alongside connections within the Whampoa establishment, namely Teng Jie, to have himself receive an official commission as an admiral. Whilst ostensibly a useless position for there is no coastline to set sail from, Gui hopes that the NRA's fortune will result in him gaining proper employment. Teng Jie
Graduating from the Department of Sociology at Shanghai University, Teng Jie garnered a wide variety of experience in managing political affairs, and with radical, extreme ideology. Joining the Whampoa Military Academy, Teng Jie graduated from the 4th Infantry Department and saw service in the Northern Expedition as a common soldier. Serving as a clerk in the General Political Department of the General Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army, he slowly became disgusted with the cooperation between the CSP and KMT.\n\nLeaving China following the collapse of the Northern Expedition to study at the Political Economy Department of the Meiji Univeristy in Japan, Teng Jie decided to focus on party politics and the study of party organisation. Deeply understanding the important role political parties play in modern politics, Teng Jie began to believe that in order to save China, it would first be needed to start with party building. Analysing the internal enemies of the Kuomintang as being local warlords and the Chinese Syndicalist Party, he deemed the former very fragile, and not an issue, whilst he thought the Chinese Syndicalist Party to be one of the greatest threats to the party. It had organisation, doctrine, strategy and support of the Internationale.\n\nTherefore in order to deal with the CSP, he desired the establishment of a new \

Tang Jiyao
The much beguiled King of the Southwest, Tang Jiyao started his life on the path of a scholar. After passing the imperial exam, he travelled to Japan and studied at the Tokyo Jinbu School, joining the Tongmenghui soon after. Graduating from the Zhenwu School and serving in the Japanese Army as an intern, he was then admitted to the Japanese Army Academy in 1907, graduating the following year as a classmate of Sun Chuanfang, Liu Cunhou, Li Genyuan, Li Liejun, and Cheng Qian among others. Returning home, he served as director of the General Staff Office, instructor at the Kunming Military Academy, and commander of a regiment.\n\nOne of the leading plotters of the Double Ninth Uprising, Tang assisted Guizhou, and was elected as the province Governor in 1911. In 1913 he repressed the Second Revolution, and succeeded Cai E as Governor of Yunnan. In 1915, alongside Li Liejun and Cai E, he planned and initiated the National Protection War. Aligning with the Constitutional Protection Government, Tang led the Jingguojun until his deposition by Gu Pinzhen in 1921.\n\nReturning in 1922, he collaborated with Chen Jiongming and opposed the Northern Expedition. Attempting to take-over Liangguang after Sun Yat-sen's death, he was beaten back by Li Zongren. Around the same time, he accepted deputy leadership of the Public Interest Party in 1925, and founded the Minzhidang, or People's Government Party in 1926. Almost couped in 1927, he persevered, and managed to establish a delicate power balance in Yunnan for the years to come.

Tang Xiaoying
§YBorn:§! §L1905, in Huili County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YBackground:§! §LOnly son of Tang Jiyao, few expected Tang Xiaoying to live up to his father's example in political notoriety, and yet here he is, President of the Chinese Republic. Picking up his father's mantle, Xiaoying himself has been a democrat of no small stature within Yunnan for years. Sent to Japan to study at the Department of Economics in the Tokyo Imperial University, Tang would return to a nation in turmoil. Serving his father dutifully, Xiaoying would organise important People's Government Party grassroots meetings within the Tang Family Garden, inviting various individuals such as Zhou Xinmin, Pan Dakui and Jiang Liangfu to help further PGP party organisation.\n\nCreating the Academic Constitutional Research Association, Tang would serve as its director and push his father to explore more democratic means of governance. Proposing that before the implementation of Constitutionalism and Federalism, the people must be granted freedom of speech and personal freedom, parties should be allowed to organise, and that the government should thus cooperate with the opposition, Xiaoying would develop a close relationship with the China Democratic League.\n\nHead of the Yunnan Provincial Party Committee of the People's Government Party, Xiaoying is unique in that he has cultivated close ties not only with Luo Longji and Wen Yiduo, but that of the Young China Party too, effectively bridging the political gap between opposition and incumbency, a role he hopes to continue fulfilling as president.§!

Tang Jiyu
§YBorn:§! §L1890, in Huize County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §aTang Jiyao's Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LBrother of Tang Jiyao, Tang Jiyu graduated from the Yunnan Army Martial Arts School, and in 1912 was appointed director of the Guizhou Military Police Bureau by his brother. Following Jiyao's appointment as governor of Yunnan, Jiyu would follow him back home, and assist his brother as director of the Yunnan Provincial Police Department and commander of the guard corps. During the National Protection War, Tang Jiyu travelled to Japan, and returned in 1916 to serve as dean of the Military Academy.\n\nIn 1923, on the orders of Tang Jiyao, he marched into Guizhou to rescue Liu Xianshi, and drive out Yuan Zuming. After his success, he became Governor of Guizhou, with Liu as director of the Military Reconstruction Committee. In 1925 Tang withdrew in light of Yuan Zuming's return, and instead marched into Guangxi on the orders of his brother.\n\nFighting catastrophically against the New Guangxi Clique, he returned in defeat and was appointed as the Yunnan Army Training Director. During the February 6th coup attempt, Tang remained steadfast besides his brother, and rallied his forces to fight against the plotters. With their success, Tang rose again in a right-hand position with Tang Jiyao, against all allegations of nepotism which may dissuade him.§!\n\n§YNotes: He is sworn brothers with Xi Ziqiang and Wang Jiexiu.§!

In 1922, Sun was promoted to lead the independent regiment under direct control of Tang Jiyao, and would see service in Sichuan and Guizhou, returning to Yunnan in 1924. Thereafterwards he served as the director of the Yunnan Tobacco and Alcohol Monopoyl Bureau, and then as commander of the Yunnan Provincial Military Police.\n\nDuring the February 6th Coup attempt by Zhang Ruji, Hu Ruoyu, Li Xuanting and Long Yun, Sun adopted a wait-and-see attitude, which proved prudent when Tang Jiyao returned in power through the personal loyalty of his subordinates. Aiding Tang in putting down the plotters, Sun was in return promoted to director of the Yunnan Provincial Youth League General Administration, becoming Tang Jiyao's right-hand man, not counting Tang Jiyu.\n\nIn 1931, Sun was promoted to Chief of Staff of the Yunnan Army for his loyalty, and proposed to Tang a plan to radically downsize Yunnan's army. However, the idea was shelved due to pressure from the Yunnan Clique warlords.

Zhang Taiyan
§YBorn:§! §LJanuary 12th, 1869 in Yuhang County, Zhejiang Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cPeople's Government Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LOne of China's greatest reformist politicians and the father of the Federalist movement, Zhang Taiyan, also known as Zhang Binglin, descended from a wealthy scholarly family. After a minor speedbump in his scholarly career, he pursued his studies under various intellectuals and philosophers. In 1894 he donated money to the reformist Qiangxue Society, and began correspondence with Kang Youwei and Liang Qichao. Serving as chief editor of Shiwu Bao on Liang's invitation, he was editor for only 4 months before engaging in a fistfight over Confucianism.\n\nEngaging with more conservative reformists there afterwards, he fled following the end of the 1898 Hundred Days' Reforms, and worked as a reporter in Japanese Taiwan. Sympathising with Kang and Liang, he met Sun Yat-sen through Liang in Tokyo, and began to focus intensely on Anti-Manchu writings. Engaged with the Tongmenghui, he advocated revolutionary morality, and splitted from Sun in 1909. After Xinhai, he briefly assisted Yuan Shikai before being imprisoned by him, and only left for Shanghai after Yuan died in 1916.\n\nIn 1917 he launched the Constitutional Protection Movement with Sun Yat-sen, and urged Tang Jiyao to take a leading role. Opposing peace talks between north and south, he began to advocate federal autonomy in 1920 alongside Xiong Xiling and Zhang Shizhao, and continually hoped that Beiyang would reform for the better, even in light of the Kuomintang. Helping to found the People's Government Party in 1926, he is one of Tang Jiyao's biggest intellectual inspirations.§!\n\n§YNotes: As one of the Founding Fathers of the Federalist Movement, and one of the last of the Old Reformers, his career has been exemplary.§!

Wang Rongbao
§YBorn:§! §L1878, in Wu County, Jiangsu Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cPeople's Government Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LAt the age of 15 Wang Rongbao was recommended to study at the Nanjing Academy, and later took the imperial examination, which led him to enter the Ministry of War. After the failure of the 100 Day Reform Movement of 1898, Wang asked for leave from his position and returned home. Becoming a teacher at the Nanyang Public School in Shanghai, he travelled to Japan to study at Waseda University and Keio University in 1901, majoring in Law and Politics.\n\nParticipating in the Youth Association's establishment, a proto-Tongmenghui organisation, he gradually transitioned to a reformist mindset, and returned to China to serve in the bureaucracy. A core figure of the constitutionalists in Beijing and a member of the Progressive Party, he assisted Yuan Shikai in the dissolution of the Qing. Serving as a member of the Provisional Senate and later the Assembly, he became Minister to Belgium, a member of the Constitution Drafting Committee, and a representative to the Spa Peace Conference.\n\nHe was then successively appointed Minister to Switzerland, and to Japan in 1922, before ultimately resigning from his position in 1932 in protest of the Shanghai Uprising's treatment. An associate of Liang Qichao, Wang is committed to reformist politics, and the advocacy of a constitutionalist government most represented by the People's Government Party.§!
Dong Ze
§YBorn:§! §L1888, in Yunlong County, Yunnan Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §cPeople's Government Party§!\n§YBackground:§! §LIn 1907 Dong Ze entered the First-Class Agricultural School of the Yunnan Imperial Academy, and the following year was granted government funding to study in Japan, entering the Tokyo Tongwen College. Returning to Yunnan he would serve as the secretary to Cai E, and was recommended by him to study in the United States.\n\nEntering Columbia University in 1912 to study politics, economics, and education, he would return to Yunnan to participate in the National Protection War, serving as secretary to the National Protection Military Governor's Office, and liaison to Hong Kong. After the NPA's victory, he returned to the United States to obtain his Master's Degree.\n\nReturning to China in 1920, he would become Director of the Prep Office of Donglu University in 1922, and Director of the Education Department. Hiring many well-known figures to work at the university, he advocated democratic school management, and various other progressive educational reforms. Dong would join the People's Government Pary in 1926 at its founding, and continue his role as Director of the Education Department.§!
Xu Yun
§YBorn:§! §L1864, in Jinjiang County, Fujian Province, Great Qing§!\n§YAlignment:§! §aTang Jiyao's Clique§!\n§YBackground:§! §LOriginally born as Xiao Guyan, Master Xu Yun would develop a deep affinity and interest in Buddhism from a young age. At the age of 17 he would be married to two wives by his father in order to prevent him from becoming a monk, however he nonetheless became one at Yongquan Temple in Fuzhou, alongside his wives. Touring much of the nation and Buddhist world in the early 1900s, Xu Yun would mediate confrontations between the Shanghai Buddhist Association and the Nanjing Datong Association in 1911.\n\nMeeting Sun Yat-sen, to discuss the revitalisation of the Buddhist Association's charter, he would travel to Beijing to meet Yuan Shikai, and have the Buddhist Association of China reorganised into the Chinese Buddhist Federation. A close associate and advisor to Cai E, he would negotiate a peaceful resolution to a Yunnanese-Tibetan War in 1913, and in 1920 he would rebuild the Huating Temple in Kunming.\n\nWell respected and admired by Tang Jiyao, Xu Yun has a token voice in Tang Jiyao's metaphorical court, with the latter always at least considering his wisdom.§!\n\n§YNotes: His actual birthdate is of poor documentation.
