Resolute in Ideals
Our men in our army are our most important aspect, for without them, the very core of the army would not exist. However, the ideal soldier should be foolhardy, concrete, and resolute in their social, economic and political ideas. Instilling these virtues into our soldiers will grant them boundless confidence in our military strategies, and our ability to apply them.
Officers' Prerogative
As exhibited by the independent units of the National Revolutionary Army — those whom originate from Whampoa at least — the delegation of local autonomy to the commanders of these units has proven remarkably successful in the past. By emphasising lower level officer initiative and independence, whilst maintaining a methodical approach to careful preparation and planning of operations, our military objectives are sure to be achieved.
Extensive Reconnaissance
Critical to triumphing over a superior enemy is waging the war of intelligence. By performing proper reconnaissance on enemy units before engagement, we are sure to be able to identify their weakpoints, and strike where it will hurt them most. However we are not merely limited to scouting detachments and binoculars, for the incensed local populace can also be utilised, providing intel on warlord forces.
Fighting in Our Favour
The National Revolutionary Army has long learnt the harsh lessons imposed on it following the collapse of the Northern Expedition. The tactics of Whampoa were not enough to outfight the German military behemoth, and the National Revolution suffered for it. Ultimately, we must utilise all necessary levers in a battle to pitch them in our favour, and by entrapping enemy columns in our land, we are sure to surround and annihilate them.
Committed in Ideology
Commitment to the party, to the ideology of the Three Principles, utmost dedication to the National Revolution, these are all attributes that our soldiers should be the most premier examples of. By instituting mass meetings explaining the political and military situation, we shall provide a sense of purpose for our soldiers, hopefully increasing their motivation in battle, allowing them to see the mission to its conclusion.
Renewed Officer Examinations
By instituting a series of exams and tests for our officer corps, our generals shall assess them on their knowledge of regulations, orders, and the modern mobile tactics of the army. Simultaneously, they must display skills in both drill and field operations. Alongside that, their personalities and proclivities will also be assessed, alongside their squad management skills, leadership in battle, and their abilities to teach, or train.
The Endpoint of Chinese Armies
Ultimately, our army structure is nothing revolutionary, despite the nomenclature. Our way of waging war is merely the continued innovations of Chinese armies following the implementation of the New Army reforms of the late Qing. From Qing, to Beiyang, to Party State, to now, our army has proven the most effective as it contains the concise capacity to implement its ideals without fear.
Extolling Political Objectives
In his service from the National Protection Wars, Zhu De has discerned the integral importance of keeping a clear focus on the overall political objectives of a war, even if they conflicted with immediate military imperatives. Cai E withheld his full strength on the eve of war, in order to rally the cause of National Protection to the provinces of Guangxi, and Sichuan. Similarly, we must prioritise the masses, before military successes.
Concentration of Popular Will
An important and often overlooked aspect of military success in the Warlord Era is that of winning the support of the civilian populace. For the average Chinese soldier is seen as nothing more than a legalised bandit. However if we display that our army is a people's army, here to liberate them from the clutches of warlords, they are sure to support both our administration and our soldiers.
Frontlines Everywhere
As argued by He Yingqin, Chinese forces must \
Improving Our Soldiery
The composition insofar of our army is comprised majority of peasants, followed by National Revolutionary veterans, then workers, and finally bandits. Such a military, whilst true in our image as a people's army, ultimately yields itself to a mixed force of varying skill levels. If we are to truly transform ourselves into a national army, we must work to standardise drills and training methods.
Installing Discipline
Born as an army comprised of the people, it is no surprise that in tense and chaotic situations, our soldiers lose their composure and exact petty revenge upon gentry and landlord alike. Despite their personal convictions, the National Revolutionary Army should be an army for the people, no matter their status in life. By instituting strict disciplinary measures, our men should learn to stow their hatred.
Strategic Defensive Tactical Offensive
Evidenced by the genius of von Schlieffen within the First Weltkrieg, and with Zhu De's own studies of the former's military theory, staying on the defensive whilst going on the offensive at operational and tactical levels is sure to win victory no matter the situation. Achieving the annihilation of enemy forces through encirclements, our army will triumph over imperialist or warlord alike.
Qualities of a Leader
Truly, the virtues of our army are emboldened and reflected by the virtues of its leadership. Ultimately, what the army desires is an aim-conscious leader, with an iron character, and an obstinate will for victory. Nothing exemplifies this more than the leadership of the National Revolutionary Army, continuously struggling for China's salvation. With suave leadership, our troops will clearly understand the issues at stake.
Lower Level Autonomy
Exhibited by the National Revolutionary Army, and by the German Army's Auftragstaktik, or Mission-type tactics, our army's theorist desire the delegation of lower level tactical concerns towards various subordinates. By defining a clear overall objective, timeframe, alongside the forces necessary for completion, the generals shall leave the officers to decipher the best way to achieve said goal.
Maintaining Flexibility
The contingent nature of war is well appreciate by our military theorists, all too familiar that tacticians and strategists alike should be familiar that the battlefield situation can radically change, and so set rules are impossible in commanding troops. Battlefield decisions should depend on the specific task at hand, the enemy's situation, and the terrain. As all of these can often change, one must be capable of being flexible with their planning.
A Hundred Regiments
All we need is 100 regiments. With 100 regiments, 200,000 men strong, we can engage any foe and devastate them. The might of the National Revolutionary Army has far ascended that of the Northern Expedition, and should any foe face it now, be it Japanese, German or otherwise, they will fear the White Sun, Blue Sky, and Wholly Red Earth. Not buckling under the cruelty of this world, our soldiers continue to push forward, continue to scream out, and continue to fight.
Reorganising the Air Force
Originally established as the Aviation Department in 1922, the Yunnan Aviation School is one of the earliest aviation schools in the whole of China. Attached to Kunming Military Academy, it would be reorganised into the Yunnan Air Force in 1924. With the funding now available to revitalise the institution, it is time for a second reorganisation of the air force, the appointment of new air captains, and the drafting of a new aviation team.
Renovating Wujiaba Airport
Wujiaba Airport, constructed under the auspices of Tang Jiyao in 1923, is one of the first airports on the mainland Asian continent. Built in a strategic location not too far from Kunming, it is the third largest airport in China, second only to the Beijing Nanyuan Airport and the Hangzhou Xianqiao Airport. However it has entered a state of disrepair, and is in dire need of both attention and funding to be brought back to its full potential.
Mass Proliferation of Airfields
Whilst Wujiaba provides its service amicably and with great capacity, Yunnan's topography is mountainous and ragged. If we are to truly reach every dark crevice of the province, and beyond into neighbouring provinces, it would be wise to engage in a wide campaign of mass airfield proliferation. By mandating that counties are to complete the construction of an airport within a time limit, albeit with no monetary compensation, we are sure to establish concrete air control.
Equalisation of Pilots
In the first class of students at Wujiaba, Tang Jiyao specifically selected two girls from wealthy families in Yunnan to enrol in the school, in an attempt to encourage students to apply, and to set a precedent for Chinese women to study aviation. However Xia Wenhua and Yin Yuejuan were not the only successful female pilots to graduate, for the third batch of graduates had 9 women in it. We must once again allow female pilots to fly, for the eventual equalisation of gender.
Powering on Liangguang
With our seizure of the twin provinces of Guangxi and Guangdong, we have found ourselves upon a cornucopia of wealth and industry, merely waiting to be resuscitated. With arsenals such as the Guangxi and Guangdong arsenals, we are sure to revolutionise not only our civilian industry, but our military industry too. With the funding of Liangguang, our Yunnan Army shall no longer be wedged in by lack of armaments, or pay.
Foreign Naval Experts
Realistically, having been an inherently landlocked province, it is an undeniable reality that our naval staff is particularly lacking. With spare funding provided by our new geopolitical situation, it would be prudent to seek out exiled, or unemployed seafarers from the Legations, to train our own naval staff in the art of naval warfare.
Securing a Merchant Marine
Without seafaring access, the Yunnan Provincial Government has traditionally relied upon land transport lines through Guangxi, Guizhou and Indochina in order for our exports to reach international markets. However with the seizure of a coastline, we can now work towards the establishment and purchase of a flotilla of ships, capable of traversing the seas in order to export and import goods from international markets.
The Lightning School
With a long tradition in the navy, owing to the ancient Cantonese naval tradition, Admiral Ouyang Ge has sought the establishment of his own naval academy within Guangdong, known as the \
A New Class of Wujiaba Cadres
With the renovation of Wujiaba airport, and the establishment of further airfields all throughout our territory, it is time to once more welcome a new generation of Wujiaba cadets into the training course. Tutored by old and new cadres alike, this new generation will perhaps see the most live combat out of any, and must be capable of rising to the challenge. For in the endurance of hardship, lies the basis for reform.
Securing Modern Equipment
Having had to rely on the, quite frankly, paltry arms and ammunition it could acquire from foreign sources and the Kunming Arsenal, the Yunnan Army has been in a dire need for guns for as long as it has been a military force. With the seizure of Canton however, the prime real estate and industries within the Pearl of the Southwest, capable of supporting the militaristic Old Guangxi cliques, is more than enough to sustain the Yunnan Army.
Integrating Beiyang's Legacy
Having long been experts of sailing the high seas, and recently without employment, the Beiyang admiralty has forever remained an amicable accompaniment of sailors compared to most of their Beiyang counterparts. Apolitical, or even harbouring sympathies for our cause, we can utilise contacts and connections with these old sea dogs, and use these men for their know-how and skills, ultimately benefiting the nation.
Defending China's Coastline
Long and contiguous, the Chinese coastline is the perfect set piece for any potential invasion from the sea. A constant issue in all applications of our defensive stratagems, some of the admiralty and army staff have advised the government to restructure and consolidate the current coastal defences, whilst also allocating funding to coastal defence ships. With these efforts, it is hoped that our coastline will become an impenetrable fortress.
Circumnavigating the Blockade
For all of its expansiveness, Chinese geography is ultimately a cage, penned in by the Japanese and Germans. With their holdings in South East Asia, and off of our immediate coastline, it is impossible for any trade goods to pass without their knowledge. Instead of simply lying down and accepting our fate however, it is crucial that we develop strategies and ships capable of evading enemy patrols, in order to circumnavigating any blockade.
A Central Aviation Academy
With the consolidation of the majority of China, Yunnan's trendsetting in the space of Chinese aviation is allowed to fully flourish. Despite notable attempts from prior regimes such as the Zhili, Fengtian or the Kuomintang, China has never truly exhibited a true Central Aviation Academy for the air force. With renewed efforts however, and the consolidation of previous attempts, our forces shall all fly under the newly christened CCAA.
Constructing Aircraft Plants
Despite ambitions to build an air force of our own, the Chinese aircraft industry is critically lacking for our needs. For a truly independent airforce, we cannot rely on foreign suppliers to meet our needs. With plans to construct an aircraft plant at Dongshan, and to expand the plant at Shaoguan, our aviation staff have further drawn up plans to establish a plant deeper within Guangxi.
Adopting Armoured Assaults
In the era of modern warfare, two things triumph above the mere mortality of mankind. The aircraft, and the tank. Roaring metal behemoths strike fear into any opposing soldier, and contain the firepower alongside mobility to perform encirclements of unbelievable swathes of frontline. If China is to truly survive amongst the great powers, it is imperative that it has its own armoured force.
The Nation Under Siege
The long awaited judgement hour has arrived. Despite our tenure, our civilisation of centuries, of millennia fears complete and utter destruction at the hands of the Japanese imperialists. No one is safe, be it woman or child. We all know this to be true, and with the impending doom approaching, the Chinese people must put away our squabbles, and unite in the face of adversity!
Acquiring Expertise
Despite previous acquisitions of foreign expertise, it has proven not enough for our needs. Old, and outdated, the seafarers of the legations are not fit for the state of modern naval warfare. With ambitions far beyond China, it is time to engage in diplomacy with foreign powers, and negotiate advisory missions to build up our own military strength.
Incentivising Airfleet Production
Overall, our lack in the number of planes flying over our skies and airfields has proven itself to be drastically insufficient in order to protect the Chinese airspace. Once more, with even more gravitas and effort, and a focus on streamlining aircraft production, our air fleet shall see a rapid expansion of its capabilities, to rival even that of the Germans.
A Nascent Marine Corps
Long a tradition in the Chinese Navy, for almost as long as the Republic itself, the Marine Corps of the Republic of China has existed since 1914, where it was drafted from the decaying Navy Sentry Corps, and transformed into a force capable of traversing naval landings and rivers. Providing ample support to the institution in our quest for a navy, our ships shall be supported by our army.
A Fleet in Six Years
An ambitious plan far exceeding our own expectations, the naval staff have drafted an governmental finance plan in order to propagate a fleet of 600,000 tons in 6 years. Granted the full go ahead by the government, hundreds of ships and dockyards are to be constructed, in order for the target to be met. Perhaps once more, the Chinese fleet shall reach as far as the Americas.
A Naval Guerilla War
With modern naval advancements extolling better, bigger, and faster ships, one can forget the silent advancement of submarine warfare. Transforming from tin-cans that are more likely to kill their passengers in an engagement with a larger vessel, submarines now dominate in their role at performing a sort of \
Combined Air-Land Offensives
Under the auspices of local land warfare, nothing is more capable of turning the tide than that of air support. Able to annihilate enemy fortifications, armour, and units alike, close air support planes have proven themselves repeatedly. With all future Chinese military engagements, our infantry will no longer move without the air force guiding them along the way, lighting up a path with bombing runs.

Scorched Earth Policies
As the enemy marches into the great encompassing Chinese landmass, their supply lines grow increasingly thin, tenuous, and desperate. Emboldened by our continuous retreats into the interior, it is expected that we must be able to give up whatever they may potentially prey upon in order to achieve total victory. Seeking to utilise anything and everything in the countryside before the invaders can, we will then follow through with a relentless guerilla assault.
Nation Building Through Turmoil
Ultimately, the bloodshed and turmoil of the invasion has led to a renewed sense of Chinese nationalism and brotherhood. Through the fire and flames of shared brutality, our countrymen, no longer their ideological tendencies, share in each other a common foe, and a common love for the Chinese nation-state. Brothers and sisters alike, we all partake in the common struggle, a common nation built through turmoil.

The Navy of the National Protectors
Just like the brave soldiers of the National Protection Army of old, our navy also serves to protect the Chinese people from imperialist infractions into our territory. Operating locally, the navy is a defensive one, however should needs require it, our brave sailors will be damned if foreign ships interfere in Chinese affairs and flee unscathed.
The Navy of Export Militarism
Ultimately, Yunnan's militarism is that of a unique strain, with a constant desire and need to be expanded outside our provincial borders, such aspects have migrated themselves into our broader national mindset. Our navy too, takes on such inclinations, and hopes to project its power and influence across all four oceans of the world.
Overseeing the Seas
In a combined effort between the aviation and navy wings of the military, they have devised joint technical designs for China's own deployment of naval bomber capabilities. To be launched from airports or carriers in order to support our navy, the integration of the third avenue of warfare is sure to result in complete domination on the naval field.
Unified Air Doctrine Cohesion
As bright and shining as ever, our air force has exhibited resounding success, yet many observers of pilot test flights have critiqued the disarray in doctrine practised by individual units. A spectre from previous attempts at regional Chinese air forces. Ultimately, if we are to eradicate such a ghost, it would be prudent to centralise our air doctrine into a coherent unified one, understood and implemented by all endeavouring pilots.
From Above and Below
Whilst our air force is increasingly capable of defending the Chinese population from terror and strategic bombing, there are times, rare as they might be, where a bomber could slip through and wreak havoc on villages and industry alike. In these times, it is up to our soldiers, to man newly founded anti-air installations, and shoot down the intruders upon our airspace. From above and below, may all those who intrude fear retribution.

Harness the Might of the Yunnan Army
The Yunnan Army has a proud history, the stalwart vanguards of southwestern China against European imperialism and defenders of Chinese republicanism against monarchist restorationists and socialist revolutionaries. It provided order amid the chaos of the 1910s, but suffered humiliating defeats in the 1920s. No more. The proud heirs of Cai E and Kunming Military Academy must rise to the occasion once again!
Awaken the National Revolutionary Spirit
The National Revolutionary Army was founded in 1925 by Dr. Sun Yat-sen himself, a force loyal to the party and the people rather than warlords and tyrants. Though defeated in the Northern Expedition and forced into an ignominious exile in Guizhou, the brave soldiers that remain have not yet forgotten their revolutionary mission. And they will do their duty until the bitter end!
The Federalist Revival
He has done it again! The Master of the Eastern Continent has once again secured his power within Yunnan! The Federalist Champion, undefeatable, unsurmountable! It is crucial to reassure the Provincial Assembly that the Governor has reaffirmed his commitments. Down with despotism! Down with Beiyang! Down with militarism! Up with People's Government! Up with Provincial Autonomy!
Leveraging Our Assets
Naturally, having ruled Yunnan for over three decades, Tang Jiyao and his cohort have acquired quite a wide breadth of assets within the province. Mines, factories, banks, money and power practically flow through the hands of the King of Yunnan's court. It is crucial that these funds be used to build up the People's Government Party, and prepare the generals for righteous war.
Buddhist Revivalism
A devout Buddhist, Tang Jiyao has found much commonality with his fellow People's Government Party founder Zhang Taiyan. Flirting with the Buddhsit revivalist movement, it is time that the Governor go all in. Inviting Xu Yun, a famous Buddhist Monk, into government, he shall serve the role of a spiritual advisor, as we improve the lives of the Yunnan people through Foshi, the Buddhist rite.
Joint Committee on the Gentry
The Gentry see to it that they ally with far more malleable warlords, such as Hu Ruoyu or Long Yun, but that's their own folly. Through Zhang Taiyan's Joint Committee of the Gentry, the Gentry will have no choice but to bend, or be rended, to Tang Jiyao's will. All must facilitate the Federalist future, and the end of the old order.
Elevating the Poor Masses
Noble as it may be, the Kuomintang are but vile vermin intent on abusing the masses. Soliciting their earnest support, they yearn for, they prod the masses, and then with the whirlwind of rage they have constructed, direct it at their enemies. However, Yunnan cannot be socialist; it is too poor without foreign aid. The masses instead should focus on freedom as their vice.
Completing Ma Cong's Reforms
Stalwart and capable, Ma Cong is one of the People Government Party's most astute members. Originally a civilian of Tang Jiyao's warlord Clique, his transition into domestic politics saw him as a principal negotiator at the Yiliang Conference for Tang, and as minister of Finance in 1928. Aiming to eliminate corruption, he was obstructed by warlords. With Tang's full support, let us annihilate this threat.
The Southwestern University
With the League's brutal crackdown in 1932 enacted by Qi Xieyuan, and the general decrease in free speech and democratic progress in the coastal areas, vast swathes of prestigious intellectuals fled into the interior. Circulating around Yunnan, the \
Order in Guizhou
Whilst naturally unpopular, the Liu family within Guizhou has connections stretching far and wide. Perhaps diminished in respect and prestige, that is nothing compared to official support from Governor Tang. Of course, the Governor has a long history with Guizhou, and is generally regarded as a butcher, or tyrant. But really, what choice does he have? Tang Jiyu?
A New National Protection War
Having long campaigned against over zealous militarisation (whilst maintaining an inflated army nonetheless), it would appear the time is ripe. The last bid for Canton in 1925 ending in nigh failure, but ultimately the Yunnan Clique was unprepared that time. With a decade on his back, it is time to claim Yunnan's rightful place as the King of the Southwest.
Aid Our Federalist Allies
Ever since the general collapse of the Federalist movement from its height in the mid 1920s, Yunnan has experienced a relative air of isolation. Sure, there is Governor Zhao, but apparent disagreements over the rightful situation within Guizhou has led to much dismay. But nonetheless, Federalism cannot survive on its own, and Yunnan needs allies if it is to survive.
Hold the Guangzhou Conference
Miraculously, or perhaps, even as ordained, the Yunnan Federalist have finally managed to fulfill the goal of over a decade ago. Our first gambit nearly cost us our lives, but our second proved fortuitous! With the southern political seat of power finally within our hands, it is inevitable that we must declare to the nation the revival of the Federalist movement!
A New Order in Beijing
And so the heroes of National Protection have done it. Without the constraints of the war two decades ago, without the reservations of its political leaders. A new, formal, political order has been established within the nation. One of Federalism and Democracy, not dilly-dallying and autocracy. The first to set forward this new order is none other than Tang Jiyao, and he is keen to grease the wheels of his new city.
Control Wartime Commodities
Frivolity and individualism has henceforth wrought vast defficiencies in valuable resources for the nation's war efforts, and beyond. Materiel, food, clothing, all manners of equipment are necessary for the nation's soldiers and its people, and yet hoarding has run amok. Through the proliferation of government supported organisations, private factories shall be ensured the necessary materials for their production of goods.
Revise the Tax System
Two things are for certain in life, death and taxes. Whilst this perhaps did not hold for many of the people in China's highly irregular flow state during the Warlord Era, it nonetheless has witnessed both extremes. High rates of mortality, and extensive taxes on miscellany and absurdities. Through a thorough revision of the taxation system, progressive taxation can be adopted, providing the government with necessary funding to substantiate itself.
China's New Industrial Revolution
All around China are situated many enemies who would see to it that it remains in ruin, that much of the country remains an easily exploitable backwater, disunited and fractured. But China's patriots, its people, its rulers and its esteemed enlightened few have developed the anathema to her enemies. Industrialisation, encompassing both light and heavy industry, will be all that the nation needs to secure its national defence forevermore.
Protect The Landowners
We seek not to deprive the people of their property, the gentry of their rights, to shuttle them onto their untimely demise as the result of masses of the dissatisfied. That is unruly, and above all else abhorrent. We seek not violence, but change, and as such private property must be held up in principle. Disputes in territory must be arbitrated fairly, and landowners assured of their importance to the state.
Encourage Resource Extraction
China is a nation full of bountiful resources, from ores, to crops, to workers, to culture, the nation of thousands of centuries undoubtedly possesses enough resources to see itself dominant on the world stage. But, as it currently stands, much of its bountiful beauty is misutlised by miscreants and capitalists intent on making a buck at her expense. Resources that can be used in public interest should be owned by the public servants.
Finding a Third Way in China
Between revolutionaries and warlords, those who are proponents of reformism have found themselves sidelined and sandwiched between vocal demagogues who seek radicalism as the solution to the nation's woes. But it is the Third Way, that of the Moderates, that of moderate opinions based on calculated evidence, expressing themselves with moderate words only, that shall save the day, and the nation.
Rejuvenating Liberal-Conservatism
The demand for democracy, for that of human rights, for that of a national constitution, the rule of law, the freedom of thought, that of speech, the right to protest against authoritarianism, militarism, and all sorts, these are all but analienable rights for the people. It is that thereof which the Liberal-Conservatives of the Moderate Crescent Moon Society promise, and it is that thereof Tang will deliver upon.
Rule of the Outstanding
The nation cannot fall to the diatribes of unenlightened fools who believe in their own facetious self-worth. This is not a game of cards, it cannot be ruled by ideology, but instead by modern science and intellectual expertise. Through administrative competence and government by experts, the nation should be ruled by that of the most outstanding group of people, experts on political science selected through examination and elections.
The Last Stand Against Tyranny
Perhaps Beiyang's greatest folly was the failure of the Republic's own administration, legislators, and jurors to deny or prevent increasing autocracy and the complete abuse of the law; constitutions were but hashed out quickly to ensure political successes. Checks and balances, it is checks and balances between government branches, and the central government in comparison to provinces, that can avoid unwieldy tyranny in the chief office.
Strengthen Presidential Powers
The warlords believe in their own folly, that the Central Government was all but guaranteed to kowtow to their needs. But it is the needs of the people, not that of the Governors, that must be seen to. And it is a great mistake to further litigate legal warlordism through a Confederation. China has grown past the need for provincialism, and it is time for a wise executive, of decisive action, to cut through the quagmire of provincial politics.
Elevating the Nation's Thinkers
Rule of the enlightened, or rule of the elite few? Parties of the masses would see to it that the tyranny and evil of the masses overpower that of those best suited towards governance. Democracy must be cultivated, not thrust unto people ill-prepared to utilise it. And so it is under this rule that the nation's brightest and most well-equipped must be elevated, shouldering the burden of the nation's future.
Integrate the Beiyang Bureaucracy
Idealists and utopians would cast aside the whole \
The Fight Against Imperialism
The most vile evil extracted upon the nation is that of the great onset of imperialistic endeavours within China. For it has bore witness to foreign powers carving it up senselessly into zones of influence and control. Even now, embroiled in war undoubtedly, they look towards the Middle Kingdom with hunger in their eyes, and malcontent for its people. It is not war between individuals, but that of nation states, and only the strong survive.
Promises of Constitutional Rule
It may seem but an empty slogan, propagated by warlords and lesser men, but our assurances are genuine, and our actions shall vindicate the new Federal government. This is not the rule of tyranny, or of a party state, but of servants of the people. Relinquishing their lives to the service of solidarity and the people's representation, to upholding laws, to upholding good morality!
Groundwork for a Confederation
Zhang Taiyan, one of the key architects of Federalism, proposed to that of which the form Chinese Federalism should take: a confederation. And alas, many would indicate that such a stance is in opposition to his desire to eliminate warlordism, but in essence it is the very support base by which warlordism can be prevented. If appeased with a confederation, they will merely not notice the curtailing of their power, and eventual removal.
Affirm Governor Loyalty
Of course, loyalty has its own rewards. It is loyalty that guarantees trust, and it is loyalty that build genuine strength amongst compatriots. As much as it is true in the military, or in daily life, loyalty serves its purpose in statecraft all the same. Not necessarily does it have to take the form of corruption either, as those who are loyal may remain. Those who are disloyal will but merely have their flames extinguished.
First Among Equals
The Province that spawned it all, the province that has safeguarded the merits of republicanism since 1911, and the republic that has championed undiluted Federalism for decades. It is Yunnan, the First Among Equals, that has shown the strengths of the provincial unit. Perfectly sized, the province is neither too big nor too small, and individually has the potential to unite the nation. Together, collective provincial might will overcome imperialism.
Unity Through National Essence
You can hardly impose your will upon others, and much similarly one cannot impose central government authority upon that of provincial rights and attitudes. As if cultivating a plant, you must take great care, and be gentle, for any overt action and it wilts away. United by common culture, Buddhist identity, and a common national essence, the backbiters of regionalism will be restrained by that of patriotic pride.
Healing the North-South Rift
For as long as it has been certain, there has been a simmering cultural and political divide between the nation's south and north. Apathetic to authoritarianism, and predisposed to invasion, the North has long since upheld both the traditional seat of power, and that of political arrangements. The South, beset with militaristic tendencies and revolutionary idealogues, has spurned great change and transition. The solution? The proper deliberation of powers.
For a New China, For a New Economy
With the seizure of Beijing, the state has had to undergo a perhaps ill-timed and radical transition as various facilities, departments, companies and other aspects of the economy were put under direct state control. With the lessening of restrictions, it is crucial that wartime controls and monopolies be abolished, and the economy reconverted back to fulfilling the needs of the people, not of the military.
Emerging From the Ashes
Individual and collective group action is not necessarily enough as it would seem to subdue the woes of the people. In various recently conquered areas and even at home, they languish and suffer under infrastructure devastation, and the collapse of monetary value. Only through direct government aid to those wanting to renew their lives, and to the Chinese yuan, can the nation truly arise from its sorry state.
Promoting Economic Security
It is one of the most important values of any free economy in the modern era that the principle of economic democracy is upheld. Under such a principle, adequate livelihood and economic securty must be ensured, and so too shall the equalisation of wealth and the further closing of the gap between the rich and the poor. The people yearn for a better life, and it is the responsibility of the government to facilitate such.
Revolution of the Middle Classes
Naturally, this is not a revolution of the masses, or of the elites, but of the middle classes. That of the producers, of the entrepreneurs, of the bounding capitalists taking risk and initiative in their endeavours. And so too should production between increased, under adequate planning from both private and national firms. It is the expectation that they hold to this proposal, and the government is obliged to assist however it can.
Sanction Safe Progress
The whirlwind of progress has never been further propelled than it has by that of the masses' fury. For it is their very yearning for a better life that has thrust upon the Chinese nation, and elsewhere, that of revolution. Unmitigated oppression can only lead to the explosive counter-attack of revolutionaries, but if you are smart in statecraft, you can alleviate such ills. Safeguarding and guaranteeing the rights of peasants and workers is but the first step to emancipation.
Federalist Fortress in the Southwest
With the return of Federalism as a formidable force in the wake of the Zhili Collapse, there have been many considerations as to the role Yunnan should play in the emancipation of the Centralist system. In its true essence, Yunnan has long been a fortress of defiance. One against tyrants, against autocrats, against monarchists, and against revolutionaries. And so it is only natural that it become a fortress of Federalism; its true safeguard.
Support the Southern Government
Playing second fiddle is hardly the place of the Yunnanese, but make no mistake, if the Southwestern Federalist government falls, Yunnan itself will be so terribly alone. We know too well the value of good allies in the Chinese battlefields, and so it is imperative that the provincial government muster all that it can to assist our allies. Troops, men, materiel, all must be put forward to our shared goal.
Press for Unification
It would appear that our ever gracious allies have deemed it fit to kick their feet around, hardly pursuing the course of unification in a genuine or timely manner. This, simply, cannot stand. The world will not wait around for the Chinese people to unite and for the nation to compose itself, and the longer we wait, the stronger our national and international adversaries become. We must press our allies to press forward with a grand offensive.
Last Holdout of Federalism
And so it would seem that history has repeated itself for the third time in the Warlord Era. Yunnan, standing on its own bare feet, must face off against an onslaught of opponents, rallying the banner of freedom, liberty, and democracy. And if history is correct, then it will be Yunnan that will undoubtedly persevere and emerge victorious. We must put forward all of our strength, all of our might, to preserve all that which we hold dear. Wansui!
Rein in the Defence Commissioners
Backed into a corner, Tang Jiyao had been forced into enabling vast amounts of Yunnan to effectively sport their own regional kingpins in the form of the Defence Commissioners. Evenly split north, west, and south of Kunming in Zhaotong, Dali, and Mengzi, the Defence Commissioners have been able to exert undue influence on Yunnan Clique policy ever since the tumultuous 1920s. They must be brought to kneel before the king.
Self Government Training
Very few existing bureaucrats and magistrates are thoroughly educated enough on the political stance on Federalism, or that of the way of local self-government. By sending cadres to the College of Law and Politics, or even abroad to places such as Japan, the government can train the old officials on the proclivities of their status, and a generation of new officials, with the general hope that they will be able to sufficiently empower local assemblies.
Second Southwestern Conference
Ostensibly it is Yunnan's allies who lead the charge of the national Federalist movement, but in the grand reality of the Federalist project, it is the Yunnan that will steward the Southwestern provinces into a cohesive and unified front. This is our destiny, and hardly anyone could oppose us. Calling forth delegates representing all aspects of the Southwest, we shall lay out the role Yunnan is to play in National Federalism.
The Yunnan Monroe Doctrine

Implement Social Reforms
With peace secured outside the provinces, Yunnan now has the bandwith to pursue a modicum of necessary reforms as the military takes a backseat. Various antiquities remain within Yunnanese cultural society, such as a despotic penal system, or ludicrous marriage, burial, and gift-giving customs. Whilst we truly do not desire to tell the people what they should and should not do, we can at least prevent the most harmful excesses of these habits.
Spreading Popular Education
It is not enough to merely construct the grand Southwestern University, or to host a whole splendor of Chinese intellectuals. Across all levels, Yunnan must be enlightened. Through the spread of popular education, the construction of primary schools, vocational schools, night schools, teacher-training schools, and promulgation of lecture societies, Yunnan will become a utopia in the Southwest.
True People's Government

Reform the Militia System
The Baojia militia system, and all other similar systems, were devised to serve as local guardsmen, or garrisons, of their respective communities. However, in-effect they have become nothing more than mere pawns of the local magistrates or gentry, aiding in the perception of their tyrannical rule over the peasantry. By consolidating and managing the militia through a central office, they will all become accountable to the governor, at least, indirectly.
Consolidate the Southwest
Under the auspices of local self-governance, it is ostensibly in poor taste to annex, or otherwise control a neighbouring province via military intervention or otherwise. As is the heart of Federalism, provinces must be ruled by their fellow provincials. However, the Guizhou experiment has shown that tying provinces together can yield considerable benefits, if applied correctly. Let us export the Dian-Qian model to the whole Southwest!

Root Out the Socialists
It has become evidently clear that vanquishing the Kuomintang was not enough to prevent Yunnan from following to the tyranny of demagogues and the masses. Preaching their poison in underground cells, various revolutionary groups remain active within Yunnan, not especially those led by Wang Fusheng or Li Xin. Socialist revolution has no place within China, it is simply too agrarian and poor for its means. If they cannot see sense, then they will see the sword.
Seize Federalist Leadership
It would appear that not all ties are made to last, and most certainly not all allies. Unfortunately, Yunnan is rather used to having to fulfill its duty and service alone, and by its own hands. With the dashing of the previous torchbearer of the Federalist movement, it is only within the due line of succession that Yunnan, and Yunnan alone, sit atop the throne of the United Provinces.
Refuge for Intellectuals
With the Crescent Moon Society and the Southwestern University establishing their roots within Yunnan, the province has somewhat turned into a cornucopia of intellectualism and development within the Chinese nation. Of course, it is only prudent that the provincial government sponsor, fund, and cultivate these ambitious modern Scholar-Officials, for their benefit, and our own.
Patriotic Labour Unions
Unions are a special, and in notion, glorious, form of representing those who form the bedrock of industrial society. It is only natural that they retain their influence and serve their role within China's industrial revolution. But they cannot be political. That sullies their potential, poisons the well of the worker's revival. No, they must be apolitical, fueled not by domineering politicians, but by pure patriotism.
Addressing the Currency Crisis
Naturally, civil war, national unification, and an all-out struggle against foreign imperialists is not particularly the ripe grounds for economic development or fostering business ties. Worse still, Yunnan itself has been in the wild throes of an influx of various currencies. German marks, Fudian bank notes, and even some lingering Yuan Shikai and Pre-Xinhai bills. By cultivating the Fudian Bank however, a solution might be found in its expansion.
Gathering Capital and Labour
Perhaps as a consequence of the Provincial Administration's rather heavy-handed approach to the labour movement, it has been utterly bereft of Chinese workers to finance its ambitious development projects. Modernisation of transportation, agriculture, mining, and light industry necessitates manpower. With workers from Vietnam and Hong Kong, alongside a worker housing scheme for native Chinese immigrants, Yunnan will develop to rival that of even Shanghai.

Push for Economic Revival
Utterly damaged by nigh-perpetual warfare since Xinhai, and banditry before that, the Chinese economy is foreign dominated, fractured, and particularly lacking in various provinces. But in order to move mountains, the Chinese must be able to assert true economic prosperity and independence. If the people and politicians do not see the true imperative of economic reconstruction, then we must but merely enlighten them.
Freedom's Final Call
The witching hour is upon us! Those traitorous cutthroats, our once auspicious allies, they seek to betray their very own ideals! To sunder it for their own grandeur and folly! This cannot stand! The martyrs of Federalism did not fight for a strong, free, and fair democracy to see it sunk by aspiring autocrats and their milieu of faceless bureaucrats. Yunnan's destiny is to be the vanguard against tyranny, and so it must be that we pick up arms and advance against our foes!
A Patriot's War
There is no true Chinese patriot that can merely sit on the sidelines and abide as the nation falls into the cataclysmic void of despotism and authoritarianism once again! This war is a people's war against a system that has spiralled out of their control. It's a war against the very forces of entropy. It's a war for the future of not just the current generation, but every generation thereafter. And it is the duy of every Chinese to fight for their freedom.
Exploiting Divided Loyalties
The traitor's own backlines and headquarters are not truly united, this much is evident in their campaigns conducted before and after their betrayal. If we but merely consolidate our own forces, and curry favour with those considering defection, or those perceiving the same injustices with their own very eyes, the traitor's ranks will break, and their resolve will be all but hollow.
Leadership of the Best and Brightest
It is the Kunming Academy that has produced some of the nation's most fantastic and brilliant generals, officers, and commanders. Staffed by an even greater body of military educators, it is the very pride of the nation, inspiring duty, honour, service, and patriotism within its alumni. Without a doubt, the Yunnan Clique is stronger for it, and so it is the Yunnan Clique's officers that will bring forward steady victory.
The Lessons of Fire and Blood
Chinese history has been bathed in bloodshed, civil war, and destruction for centuries. Our revolt is but one in a long-line of defiant stands against national tyranny and despotism. But it will not be a failure. In recent history, in Xinhai and the war for National Protection, Yunnan was the trendsetter on securing victory, and it is only natural that these past victories propel us further.
Sustaining the Republic's Flame
Aspiring for democracy, freedom, and Federalism are noble goals. It is the true Utopian idealism of the Chinese masses that they too, like their compatriots in the West and elsewhere, can assert the popular mandate of election and recall. It is the very roaring flame that bore witness to the flourish of the Chinese republican revolutionaries, and it is this very flame that we have protected, and ultimately, set ablaze.
No Sacrifice, No Victory
You cannot secure victory without some form of sacrifice. The martyrs of revolution and reform have vindicated their struggle with loss of life, and it is through this fight against tyranny that the Chinese people must again muster their willpower, vanquish the autocrats, and ensure lasting peace within the Republic. No matter the cost, China must be united, and it must be a democracy.
The Fight for Human Rights
It is only under the continued campaign for one's own indomnitable human rights that a Free and Democratic political system can emerge;this has long been the core of the Crescent Moon Society's platform. A state cannot focus itself upon the granting of citizens rights whilst ignoring that of intrinsic human rights. Democracies all around the globe put citizen's rights first, but it will be the Crescent Moon that takes the step towards the primacy of human rights.

Many posit that the antidote to foreign imperialism is to pursue a total mobilisation of the people, to direct cultural and military throughput against Tokyo, Moscow, or Berlin. And they would be at least half-right. But it is nationalism, the forsaken adoration and pride in one's country, their history, and their culture, that will fight imperialism. Internationalism can wait, at least until all of China is ruled by the Chinese.

Leadership of the Talented Minority
The Jinshi and all other Scholar-Officials had once stewarded the Qing unto enlightened progress. Following examples set by Confucius or Mencius, they commanded the confidence of the court and that of society to be the experts of the Chinese government. Therefore it is only natural that their modern-day descendants, the intellectuals and experts, carry on their burden, staffing the central bureaucracy.
Ending the Political Chaos
Naturally the intense political chaos within China has largely been caused by two resoundingly evil forces: the militarists controlling the government and politics, and the incentivised taking of spoils by warlords, bandits, or corrupt bureaucrats. To be the anathema of such evil forces, it is necessary to both restrain the army, and flush out the bureaucracy. Squabbling politicians yield no good fortunes, and it is the government's duty to keep them in check.
Third Way Economics
China is largely an agrarian society, the peasants labour under their gentry landlords whilst few scant urban centres such as Tianjin or Shanghai shore up large portions of the urban productivity sector. To transform China it is imperative that a state-controlled economy is put in place. The state is an instrument of national development, and so both free markets and class struggle must be rejected in the name of state development.
The Peaceful Road to Socialism
As China itself is so deprived of material and economic prosperity, it is all too common-place for the destitute and the angry to look towards historical materialist views and that of the class struggle in order to achieve prosperity. But it is not economic inequality but that of political inequality which is the true wellspring of woe. To cultivate the end goal of Chinese socialism, one must induct it through the democratic process.
Spartan Education Methods
As espoused by Cun Shusheng time and time again, Chinese society, and especially its schools and universities, must be but all self-sufficient if they are to survive in harsh reality. Indebted with thousands of years of tradition and culture, students must learn to be strict, to be diligent, to be pragmatic, and open to new ideas whilst maintaining a concise and concerted core tenents that they live by.
From a Spark to a Prairie Fire
From one noble spark, a cascading revolution may erupt. Similarly, from one principled example, may a whole prairie fire roar to life. The torch of Cun Shusheng and Su Honggang, two admirable educators, shall set forth a bright era of enlightenment upon the whole country. No longer shall any descendant of the Yellow Emperor be a submissive citizen, nor shall they be a willing slave to any foreign master.
Economic Stewardship
Black Monday and annual recessions have set the clear example that Central Governments can hardly sit idly by and merely watch chaos erupt within agricultural and industrial sectors during economic hardship. China moreso demands an active hand in economic affairs; seeking peaceful resolutions to land disputes, relief of peasant suffering whilst protecting interests of landowners, free enterprise, all manner of stable economics must be managed by state hands.
Mandatory Public Education
In 1902, the Guangxu Emperor issued an edict closing all traditional schools like the Kunming Academy, and reorganising them based upon moderl principles. Two normal schools were founded, one for boys and another for girls, alongside that of the School of Mines, and the School of Law and Politics. By the 1920s, there were 10 modern schools with 2000 students. Education has been at the core of Yunnanese life, and it is imperative it become a core of Chinese life too.
Scholarly Civil Service
Truly the most admirable civil service system in the world has to be that of the United States. Setting the example, the development of the system from George Washington onward is nothing short of marvelous. In their unselfish service, both Washington and Jefferson cleaned up corruption, and ensured that the civil service remained loyal to the nation, not to any politial party. And it is to this example that China must emulate.
Modernising China
To be a truly strong nation, capable of its own independent action, China must be modern. And to be a modern state, it must be based upon the foundations of agriculture, commerce, and industry. Those three titans of which all western nations have been made wealthy and strong upon. It takes but a few confident Chinese merchants to one day forge a great commercial circle that will compete with their western counterparts.
Zhang Taiyan's Federation
Whilst not necessarily as extreme as he would've wanted, Zhang Taiyan's banner still soars high in the Capital. The spiritual father of the nation, his successors must work in order to build a balanced government that still remains feasible. Not confederation, but as autonomous as possible; provinces have power, perhaps even a national guard, but the Central Government must still retain its say.
Peace with the Democrats
Fears loom large that the People's Government Party merely seeks to install dictatorship, or a dominant party akin to those front organisations such as the Harmony Association or Recovery League, but that could be no further than the truth. Extending an olive branch, the PGP must calm tensions with not only the China Democratic League and the independent democrats, but also that of the Young China Party.

Whilst depriving the gentry of their dominance, it also comparitively deprives them of any influence at all. There must be a sense of balance, and harmony, in agrarian matters, of benevolent landlords overseeing diligent workers.
Arbiter Between the Provinces
There is no greater statesman in the whole of the modern Chinese politial era than that of Tang Jiyao. A son of revolutionary fire, and of intense patriotism, he has not only brought forward true freedom for the Chinese people, but that of true democracy. A central, binding, and neutral figure, a truly enlightened individual capable of balancing the interests of every Chinese individual. A true First Amongst Equals.
The Saviour of the Nation
Nobody could've done it as well as the Tang family has. Marching under the banner of people's government, people's democracy, and people's federalism, they have ensured both the prosperity of the Chinese republic, and the continued dominance of the Yunnanese in Chinese affairs. They were the saviours of the nation, the endeavouring soldiers that fought against autocracy, and they have done so yet again.
Demobilising the Army
It is of the utmost importance in the new Chinese federation that warlordism and its ilk be curtailed nigh indefinitely. There can never be another Warlord Era, and whilst extending autonomy to provinces, it must be assured that militarists do not gain power in such a scenario. As such, the national army must be reduced to just 200,000 men, enough for independent action whilst protecting national integrity.
Preserving Chinese Culture
Chinese civilisation has seen itself much downtrodden in recent years. A Century of Humiliation, decades of infighting and strife, a failing political system and a failing society. Much has been done to damage our thousands of years old culture, but no more! Chinese culture must be preserved, it must be handled delicately and allowed to thrive. Intertwined with Chinese Buddhism as a binding factor, neither socialist nor imperialist shall further our humiliation.

And so it is the duty of every Chinese citizen, whatever background, whatever profession, to carry with them the torch of our collective legacy, and march onwards into a new era of prosperity.
Cai E's Champion

Perhaps if he had not died early, it would've been Cai E in this very position. An apolitical First Amongst Equals, he stood against political parties. Tang can only hope he is proud.

With the Dian-Qian Showdown result in a resounding Guizhou Kuomintang victory, the likes of Tang Jiyao and his Federalist cadres have been ejected from the province. A mere shambling corpse, too stubborn to die. Yet in our despair we reflected. In our exile we contemplated our shortcomings. In our defeat we have been reborn, a new hope for the nation.
Mobilisation of the Soul
In order to reclaim the materiality of traditional values, the party has to undertake a spiritual transformation, managing the morals, habits, thoughts and ambitions of the Chinese people. Awaken the Sleeper Cells

Lighting the Match
In order to march northward from our bastion of Yunnan, it is imperative that either ourselves or our allies control the Shining Pearl of the South. For with Guangdong, the party's home of the revolution can once more serve as the cradle for a Northern Expedition. After all, national unification is the one and only objective under which everything else must be subsumed, and the National Revolutionary Army must utterly dedicate itself to such action.
Hold a National Congress
With Guangzhou secure, we have the needed legitimacy to hold a National Congress of the Kuomintang, bringing together the disparate rightist factions of the party into a cohesive revolutionary government. The ensuing task of building a working party-state will not be easy; there remain many divisions between the different wings of the party. Developing the Civilian Party
The basis of nationalism is the ethics of filial piety. The basis of democracy is the ethics of trust and righteousness. The basis of people's livelihood is the ethics of benevolence and peace. With the party now firmly re-established in its home province of Guangdong, it is time to set forth on enacting the National Revolution.
A Western Expedition

Return of the Northern Expedition

However with our strength regained, our forces rejuvenated, our men steel hearted, the time to strike northward is upon us!

Kuomintang-ising the Southwest

Cleaning out the Rot and Decadence
The incredibly dysfunctional mismanagement of Yunnan's administration by Tang Jiyao and his local feudal lords has developed a culture of corruption within the province. Built on personal satisfaction as opposed to national good, bandits and merchants run rampant, and in our rush to ensure a return of the Party to Guangzhou, we have abided by this state of affairs. Humbling the Kingmakers

Rallying the Legacy of the Southwest
Long has Kunming punched above its weight in national affairs. The Political-Military Offensive
With the Kuomintang joining hands with the Chinese Syndicalist Party in the United Front of 1924, a revolutionary sisterhood has developed between the sibling parties. Despite this however, radicals within the CSP cultivate a certain air of antagonisation with the KMT, especially within Yunnan. By directing an offensive of 70% political and 30% military endeavours, we can stem the red tide of syndicalism.
Contacting the Yunnan Labour Unions
Yunnan's own native Syndicalist union movement has long been a developing bud in the flowerbed. Slowly cultivated by the fervent Republicanism and dire conditions of previous Yunnan administrations alongside the influence of the Party, it has grown into a force to be reckoned with within the provincial scene. With our mutual ties and friendship with the CSP, let us foster a positive relationship with the Kunming unions.

All must be sent forthward towards the Central Committee to aid the flagbearers of the Kuomintang in their reconquest and unification of the nation.

Through the force of Yunnan and Guizhou, the Southwest has valiantly served the Kuomintang in all endeavours. Surely the whole Southwest is to follow.

Marx's words do not resound with the traditional aesthetics of Chinese political ethos but rather they derive nothing more than struggle and disunity between the classes.

By further ingratiating it within the provincial government's administration, Yunnan will bring all major local banks under one state-owned umbrella.
Commerce's Wartime Contribution
The Yunnan Chamber of Commerce under Miao Yuntai has long been the lifeline of Yunnan provincial economics since the 1920s. And yet with a surplus of currency, they have not contributed nearly enough to Yunnan's wartime goals. By allocating a special fund for the acquisition of guns and ammunition, Yunnan will have the latest in international weaponry at its disposal.
Militarisation to Save the Nation
Only through force of arms may the Chinese liberate themselves from foreign impression and national disunity. In the game of evolution, only the strong survive, and similarly so only nations that can impose their will upon others will be guaranteed latent security. For every rifle constructed, a bullet is loaded, and with that the nation takes one step forward.
Maximise Tax Revenues
Through the levying of a special consumption tax, and a special business tax, alongside forcibly implementing the stamp tax, Yunnan should be able to garner millions more yuan from its citizens to re-introduce into state enterprises. Furthermore, by monopolising the sale and transportation of opium, the government can both curb its influence, and rake in immense profits.
Cai E's Dream Realised
As advocated by Cai E, the spiritual successor of the present Central Government, the President should be strong, resilient, taking no stances on issues unless the principle of the central government was at stake, whislt the legislative branch should not be able to command the President or cabinet. The incumbent President certainly makes no qualms in following such a doctrine.
Obligations of the Military
The natural role of the military-man in the nation's politics is that to be a prominent participant in its nation-state building project; they are obliged to defend the nation against all threats, and thus are entitled, or warranted, to intervene in the political sphere should the nation's interest be at risk. Whilst the politicians squabble, the military must remain vigilant.
The Financial Regulation Committee
As the nation has undergone untold amounts of political and military strife, it too has been levied with severe economic collapse in multiple sectors, alongside a highly irregular state financial network. Through the establishment of a new economic regulation committee, the state shall begin its economic revival through abolishing all previous economic irregularities.
Building a Shared Nation State
It is in Cai E's ideal of a state, of a shared nation-state, that every individual assumes their respective responsibility for the well-being of the nation-state, thus ensuring its survival. To consider undermining any of the political institutions of the republic, be it through abrogation of elections, or strongarming the branches of government, would thus erode national unity.
Restoring Harmony to the Countryside
Whilst the gentry may balk at the notion, you cannot rule a nation in perpetual fear or contention with that of the masses. As Dr. Sun provided, it is necessary, in some retrospect, to see to it that Land to the Tiller be implemented throughout the nation. However, the government should refrain from politicising the masses in this programme, lest revolutionary fervour take hold.
All Under the King
As is his right, both as a war hero and the head of state, every individual minister of his cabinet should be absolutely responsible to President Long Yun; the parliament should exist to vote on the President's agenda, not the other way around. Partisan strife has no place in the new Beiyang Republic, and if any parties do exist, they should be entirely constitutionally based.
Duel of Twin Dragons
With the sundering of all other opponents, it would appear that the ensuing tide of Dian Clique backstabbing has succumbed even that of Hu Ruoyu and Lu Han. The incumbent herald of the remnants of Tang Jiyao's nation-building project, and the ambitious adventurous stalwart, once attached to Long Yun. Facing off despite their mutual victory, it would appear that the nation's strife is not over yet.
Restraining the Revolution
Soldiers should not take part in political parties, if they allow themselves to be distracted and disturbed by external matters, then the task of leading armies will fall bit by bit to civilian weaklings. Similarly, if every party had military backing, then it will become an untrustworthy institution. In principle the revolution was good, but you cannot politicise the army's men.
Three Trainings and Commandments
With the unification of the nation, there has been a grand increase in the extra-judicial rights of various middle to high ranking officers, who have become something of a new warlord class in of themselves. In order to restore strict discipline and reduce corruption, we must instill the virtues of honesty, diligence, and selflessness, and fight against all injustices.
From Flexibility to Dynamicism
Lacking in concrete ideological beliefs could be viewed as an innate sense of personalism, or lack of a state-building plan, for Hu Ruoyu and Lu Han it is perhaps their greatest strength. Staying true to the ideal of apolitical and decisive strongmen willing to make pragmatic choices, they are able to inevitably prioritise what is best for the nation, be it liberal, or conservative.
Cultivate the National Youth
Originally a pet project of the local Dian warlords, the Yunnan Provincial Youth League Affairs Bureau is the perfect model to extrapolate and export nation-wide. For the future generations need guidance, and a wise hand to induct them into steering the future of China. Thus, it is necessary to cultivate their spirit through youth leagues and other organisations.
China As a Melting Pot
Having synthesised a minority Yi armed forces with a majority Han provincial bureaucracy, Long Yun is no stranger to integrating China's various minority cultures into one broader national whole. Similarly, he has sponsored a great expanse of operas, libraries, and museums. Staying true to his origins, President Long has sought to embrace a new multicultural identity for the new cosmopolitan China.
Adherence to the New Literati
In dynasties past, the scholars were once upheld as virtuous civil servants who steered China into a direction of harmonious progress. With the Xinhai Revolution however, a new form of prestigious literati has emerged: the intellectual class. Exposed to Western ideas, or otherwise attempting to synthesise them with Chinese tradition, let us once more heed these men.
Exporting the Dian Economic Model
As opposed to Eastern China, Western China had to adopt its own form of economic development: it could not rely on foreigners to build factories and teach the workers, as they had little investments in the interior. As such, a major bureaucratic state apparatus, central planning, and government intervention within key industries ruled the day, and it shall rule the nation too.

Restoring Auspicious Governance

Revolutionary Constitutionalism
Ambivalent to the true revolutionary struggle of the Kuomintang, Lu Han nonetheless sees much merit in their ideals and practices. Reasoning with and understanding the plight of the common peasantry, and the desire for a strong, democratic, and nationalist state, Lu can call upon wise men such as Zhou Zhongyue to facilitate the re-admission of some revolutionaries into the mainstream.
The Steeled \
Close friends with many endearing democrats of all political stripes, Long Yun is at his heart a man born in the ostensibly democratic ideals of Xinhai. Whilst having ascended to the highest office at the helm of a military onslaught, President Long nonetheless prefers to rule by and through constitutionalist rule. Whilst democracy may not come soon, it can at least be an ideal to strive for.
Government By Efficiency
Democrats, demagogues, and idealogues suffer from the infallible nature of believing more in their ideological tenets than that of what is best for the nation. And it is only further admission of their faults and failures that President Long, pragmatic and erstwhile, ascended to the state office. Through the rules of efficiency and progress, China and its citizens will prosper.
Protecting China's Foundations
The Chinese nation-state is entirely beholden to its capacity to care for, control, and revitalise both its agricultural sector and the environment. Whilst the peasantry are actively seen to, it is necessary to maintain the fields they till too. Through regional conservation boards and land reclamation bureaus, China will never again suffer starvation.

Having been key backers of many individuals now close to the upper halls of the central government, the gentry have seen their position seemingly diminished in light of unification due to the nature of the peasant issue. However, it is still possible to strike a mutually beneficial deal. Protecting the gentry from instability, the government shall earn their compliance.

Initial War Preparations Are Completed
Though Yunnan and Guizhou are neighbours, laying the groundwork for an invasion will take some time. Supply depots need to be created, battlemaps need to be drawn out, and freshly arrived troops need to be positioned. On both sides of the border, generals are war-gaming their next moves, hoping to gain a critical advantage. The buildup along the frontlines continues across planting season, and by summer commanders believe their armies will be primed for an invasion.
Troops Flood to the Dian-Qian Border
The amassing of units on the Yunnan-Guizhou border has caused a cycle of continued escalation as both sides deploy forces to the front. With any hope of a surprise attack lost by this point, both sides race to try and outdo the other - ironically reinforcing the stalemate. It will only be through decisive action that one side gain a large enough advantage at the border needed to overrun the other.
Switch Sides
The Warlord Era is filled with tales of sordid betrayals, sometimes due to envy, sometimes due to greed, and sometimes for self preservation. For many of the lower ranking officers on both sides of the border, this choice has become more and more tempting as the tide begins to turn.
Commence the Assault

Accelerate Our Buildup

The side that is able to marshal the resources of its people and overcome bureaucratic inertia will be the one with more guns, more supplies, and more troops.
Develop our Battleplan
They say the best laid plans of the generals never survive contact with the enemy, but that hardly diminishes the value of a good plan. Win the War of Wills
The supreme art of war is to subdue the enemy without fighting, and in an era of shifting loyalties the effective number of troops one side has on the ground may be far fewer or far greater than their actual soldiers gathered. With tailored propaganda on one hand and some generous bribes on the other, we may be able to convince our opponents to give up or at least not resist as hard. Similarly, adequate pay and good treatment of our men will go a long way for shoring up our own officers and mens' loyalties.

Qiongya Rubber
With Qiongya's warm climate and nutrient rich soil, it has become a plantation for cash crops in recent years. Profits from the island's cash crops can be further increased if a rubber plantation is started to supply both our government and any potential foreign buyers with rubber.
Guangxi Infrastructure Development Scheme
With Guangxi often lacking behind in development, its infrastructure is often not up to modern standards. Therefore, if our government hopes to develop Guangxi's industry, investment in new infrastrucutre projects is of the utmost imporance.
Guangxi Farmers Bank
Farmers live in a cycle of perpetual debt, taking on loans in the spring in hopes of reaping a fruitful harvest in the fall. Due to Yunnan's mountainous terrain, large scale agricultural developments have always been a challenge in the region. Yunnan Water Control

Isolated politically, we should send peace feelers to Yunnan, announcing our intention of achieving national unification without resorting to forceful methods. With the promotion of peace in our mutual interest, it is no doubt Kunming will accept and align with us in the name of uniting the nation peacefully.
The Provisional Constitution Crisis
[YUN_provisional_constitution_crisis_desc_scripted_loc]
President He Yingqin has vowed to pass the Provisional Constitution, whatever the cost may be. To him, this is the only way to unite the nation and assert his authority once and for all. Faced with stiff opposition by Hu Hanmin, Premier of the Legislative Yuan, he has ordered his men to begin planning an auto-coup - eliminating dissent against his rule by force in one fell swoop.\n\nIn order to pull this off successfully, He Yingqin must ensure that §cNationalist Zeal§! remains stably in the centre: above §R$RKT_bop_unrelenting_cynicism$§! and below §G$RKT_bop_unbridled_conviction$§! at the end of the 60 day $YUN_he_yingqin_autocoup_mission$ mission.\n\nCurrently, Nationalist Zeal sits at §Y[ROOT.GetActiveRangeName]§!
In the fallout of Hu Hanmin's arrest, the Provisional Constitution Crisis has spun out of control. Hoping to salvage the situation, the §MPolitical Science Clique§! has staged a power grab, strongly opposed by their rivals in the §aCC Clique§!. Meanwhile, the §PWhampoa Clique§! are considering a coup of their own.\n\nThe National Assembly is on-going. Delegates are known to double-dealing, willing to vote with who incentivises them more or appears stronger at the moment.\n\nThe §MPolitical Science Clique§! needs §M335 Votes§! to pass their Constitution and save their government.\n[?YUN_PSC_aligned_delegates_variable|M0]§M/502§! Delegates are currently willing to vote with them.\n\nThe §aCC Clique§! needs §g252 Votes§! to reject the Constitution and begin a vote of no confidence.\n[?YUN_CCC_aligned_delegates_variable|g0]§g/502§! Delegates are currently willing to vote with them.\n\nIf a resolution is not found in time, there will be a §PWhampoa Clique§! coup d'etat.\n\nThe ultimate victor will suffer a penalty to §g£pol_power Political Power (CCC Seats)§!, §M£GFX_stability_texticon Stability (PSC Seats)§!, and/or §P£war_support_texticon War Support (Coup Time)§! proportional to the strength of their opponents at the end of the crisis.
He Yingqin's Autocoup
Mounting criticism from within the party, spearheaded by Premier of the Legislative Yuan Hu Hanmin, has created a brutal rift between Hu and President He Yingqin. As mutual suspicion grows, exacerbated by the drafting a Provisional Constitution, He Yingqin has resolved to eliminate his rival once and for all.\n\nTo do so he will need to not only purge the party of Hu Hanmin and his Moscow Committee Clique allies, but also disarm or threaten into submission the regional militarist cliques that dominate the party's southern heartland. This is no easy task, and to be successful he will need to demonstrate that he can preserve party stability and avoid allowing Nationalist Zeal from growing too high or too low.
Hu Hanmin's Outrage
Hu Hanmin is a fiery orator and one of Sun Yat-sen's closest disciples, allowing him to express an unusually large amount of dissent within the party-state. A devout democratic-centralist, he has lashed out against Kuomintang figures who have formed factions to advance private interests and government officials who hoard property and live off corruption, both understood by He Yingqin as a veiled attack on the Generalissimo.\n\nWhile his antics were once tolerable, or at least a necessary evil, the discussions over the Provisional Constitution have worsened relations between the two men. Hu, as Premier of the Legislative Yuan, argues that the Kuomintang can convene a National Assembly (also translated as the National People's Convention) but it cannot draft a provisional constitution. The National Assembly can only draft a full constitution at the end of the Political Tutelage. Moreover, Hu argues that a provisional constitution would not improve the life of the people, instead it would be a distraction from the national reconstruction, reduction of taxes, and development of communication infrastructure, agriculture, industry, and commerce.\n\nUnlike the empty words of the provisional constitution, Hu Hanmin is very much willing to back his views with his well armed supporters.

Divide and Conquer in Hunan
Hunan has a complicated relationship with the Kuomintang. Not only a major battleground between Beiyang and Guangzhou governments over the years, the populous province also was home to three feuding Kuomintang-aligned factions. Ever since the rise of the New Right, Hunan has straddled the line between obeying central government directives and expressing sympathies with regionalist and Old Right movements.
$YUN_divide_and_conquer_in_hunan_mission_intro$\n\nThey are a quasi-subordinate region anyway, so show of force should intimidate the fence sitters into aligning with our interests and their petty internal rivalries will do the rest.

Secure the Southwest
The southwestern provinces of Yunnan and Guizhou have been our military heartland for many years. It is where the National Revolutionary Army first reorganised after its defeat in the Northern Expedition and the endpoint of the Long March.
